Correspondence

To the esteemed editor: I have just read a news item in your newspaper of the 15th of this month, titled "Finance Department Forbids British-American Tobacco Company from Growing Tobacco in Xuchang." Upon investigation, the British-American Tobacco Company has not submitted a request to establish tobacco-growing facilities in Xuchang, nor has this office reported to the ministry to warn the company to cease growing. This is clearly based on inaccurate rumors. Therefore, I am writing to request that your newspaper promptly correct this matter to avoid misleading the public. Your cooperation is greatly appreciated. Respectfully, General Affairs Section, Taxation Department, Ministry of Finance. August 15th.

Furthermore, please note that "拱" in yesterday's newspaper should have been "烘." To the esteemed editor: I have examined a news article in your newspaper of the 15th of this month, under the local news section, titled "Carpenter Sues Doctor for Unwarrantedly Removing Hand." The article mentions that Lu Mingyao from Jiangdu graduated from Tongde Medical College. Upon checking, our college's past graduates do not include anyone named Lu Mingyao. This is clearly based on inaccurate rumors. I am writing to request a correction and hope it can be published in the "Corrections" column to clarify the truth. Respectfully, Tongde Medical College. August 15th.

Spring and Autumn

Tidbits

— (Xie Zhongwen)

When cleverness and foolishness are properly employed, both the clever and the foolish become admirable individuals in the world.

Cleverness teaches one to conserve effort and save time to overcome difficulties; foolishness teaches one to persist and advance bravely to overcome difficulties.

The wisdom of the clever and the courage of the foolish are both sources of all creation.

When cleverness and foolishness are improperly employed, both the clever and the foolish become detestable individuals in the world.

Cleverness becomes mere trickery, and foolishness becomes a stimulant for reckless action.

The cunning of the clever and the obstinacy of the foolish both become factors that disrupt society.

We need the wisdom of the clever, not their cunning, and the courage of the foolish, not their obstinacy.

However, in society, we only see cunning people harming others, and no foolish people willing to take losses!

Supplement to the Biography of Wang Junqing

— Zheng Yimei

The Wuxing lyricist Wang Junqing has passed away. I have already written an article to mourn him, but there are still things left unsaid, so I write again here.

When the lyricist was building his Xinjiang Villa in Wumen, before moving, he asked me to introduce him to some fellow poets, hoping for literary gatherings in the future. Unexpectedly, a rogue youth, impersonating the poet Jin Jihe, asked the lyricist for a loan. The lyricist generously lent him some money and wrote to me describing the youth's appearance, asking if he was indeed Jin Jihe. I was greatly surprised upon receiving the letter because Jin Jihe was tall and slender, with a refined demeanor, unlike the shabby person described in the letter. When Jin Jihe found out, he invited the lyricist to a restaurant to clarify the matter, suggesting he bring someone to identify the tall man to avoid confusion. This double impersonation case became a humorous anecdote among our peers.

I met the lyricist several years ago, and we became close friends at first sight, forming a friendship that transcended age. At that time, I had just suffered through the January 28th Incident, losing my home and family possessions, and my sorrow was expressed in my writings. The lyricist comforted me with sincere words, saying, "If you have any urgent needs, please do not hesitate to tell me. I will do what I can to help." I politely declined, but his kindness was truly touching.

In the early years of the Republic of China, the lyricist vowed to compile biographies of women, aiming to add glory to the female world, including figures like Qiu Jin and Hua Yinmei. Unfortunately, due to certain circumstances, this project never materialized, which is a great pity.

Zhu Minyi, a member of the Central Committee, received early guidance from the lyricist and always treated him with the respect due to a teacher. Some compared this relationship to that of Wang Zhaoming and Zhu Jiangcun, or Yu Youren and Shen Jianchao. However, the lyricist never asked for any favors, as his mind was serene and detached, with no desire for personal gain.

The lyricist was on good terms with Grand Historian Cheng Zongyi. Upon hearing of the lyricist's passing, the Grand Historian composed two poems of condolence. At his request, I am publishing them here to conclude my writing: "I admired you at first sight in Duntang, the news of your passing in Wuzhong shocked me, I am saddened by my lack of opportunity to visit your home (You repeatedly invited me to Suzhou), Your ability to proofread and your touch to improve texts are impressive (You made a living by editing books), You had hoped for a son like Xiangshan to forget aging, Our friendship can be compared to Fan Shi, to take responsibility for life, There is still a promise unfulfilled to write the epitaph on the monument for a former colleague (You asked me to write the epitaph for the tomb of Huang Jiuyan, a Ming Dynasty Jinshi, but because of the humidity, my hands were unable to finish), Tears flow to the ends of the earth as a response. The stars are lonely after dawn, I quietly think of you, Your works and scattered writings are truly pitiable, I savor the flavor of poetry in the Yun Song Collection (People in Shanghai used to say that his poetry style was from Oubei), I carefully selected content for the Xibao Editorial (Referring to the annotated Yao Xuan's Selections of Ancient Prose). We shared the waters and bamboos of the Xuan Mian Garden, The writing desk still is always the fields, How could you buried next to Yao Li's tomb and still have English wind to remember the past." The lyricist's character can be seen in these poems.

Put in Some Effort

— Juan Yin

Talking About Pointe Shoes

— Yiqiu

"Dancing can beautify all the gestures and movements of a woman," I remember an artist saying. Having been involved in the world of song and dance for many years, I have proven the accuracy of this view through experience.

Pointe dancing is the highest peak of dance art and can make a person graceful, because this type of dance is elastic. It can turn any heavy or dull woman into a light and elegant beauty. However, in China, strictly speaking, only Gong Qiuxia and Pan Wenjuan are truly capable of dancing en pointe.

Some Jianghu troupes that perform magic and martial arts will have one or two little girls come out to dance en pointe at the beginning of their performances, but that kind of leaping that only raises the heel with the front toes fully touching the ground cannot be called pointe dancing.

In foreign countries, dancing on pointe is very common. General dances are composed of pointe steps. However, in China, where all arts are pitifully lacking—dance is no exception! Pointe dancing is indeed considered precious.

According to Ms. Wei Yingbo, the reason for the scarcity of pointe dance talent is that Chinese song and dance practitioners lack perseverance. It is not easy to dance on pointe on stage for ten minutes. It requires a lot of hard work to succeed.

Ms. Gong Qiuxia has married and left the world of song and dance for many years. Only Ms. Pan Wenjuan is still making progress. She is currently performing in Southeast Asia. It is said that overseas Chinese audiences are deeply impressed and warmly welcome Ms. Pan's pointe dancing. Local newspapers have published special articles on Ms. Pan, praising her as a "Song and Dance Master" with genuine talent and skills, so popular for a while. According to someone in the song and dance industry, in Southeast Asia, the most prestigious group of Chinese song and dance is the Voice of Plum Blossom, but Ms. Pan Wenjuan is the most popular individual. This shows that true honor is not something that can be obtained by chance. It is hoped that the general female song and dance performers will not rely on luck again, thinking that learning a few flirty glances and smiles is a big deal. It must be known that in the near future, girls with only shallow skills and no real ability will be naturally eliminated.

The Amusements of Lotus Root Cottage

— (Shen Shou Ruo)

The famous scholar of Yunjian, Mr. Yang Jiyuan, was broad-minded and elegant during his lifetime. He once appreciated the scenery of the Bund in the Huangpu area and lived next door to women of the goddess profession. Mr. Yang lived there peacefully, without considering it a disgrace to dwell in such surroundings. He named his residence "Lotus Root Cottage." When people asked about the meaning of the name, Mr. Yang happily explained that he compared himself to the pure and lofty lotus root, which remains untainted even when surrounded by mud. The meaning of this residence can be described as amusing.

Little Western Paradise

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Seventeen: Do Not Ask About a Daughter's Body, Difficult to Speak of Hidden Pains, Everyone Eagerly Looks at the Face of a Noble Person, Together Admiring a Lofty Demeanor

The accountant smiled and said, "Mr. Zhang is truly meticulous, even practicing a lot beforehand." Jie Fu extended his thumb and raised his head, saying, "My handwriting is recognizable to Commissioner Lan at a glance. I haven't written large characters for more than two months, so my brushwork has regressed a bit. If Commissioner Lan arrives tomorrow and mentions that the characters were written by me, and he sees that my handwriting has regressed, I am sure to be reprimanded. There is a saying that one should not fear officials, only those who manage them. Who can help the fact that my position is lower than his?" Hearing him say such things, the accountant felt even more that he had a close relationship with Commissioner Lan. Therefore, after he finished writing the slogans, he immediately went to the front of the store to spread the word, saying that no wonder the Zhang gentleman living in the backyard was going to write slogans to welcome Commissioner Lan. It turned out that he was a subordinate of Commissioner Lan. He shouldn't have given him a bill and asked for money the day before yesterday. However, since the bill had already been given, and he hadn't paid yet, he should relax a little on him in the future. Speaking of the Little Western Paradise Inn, it often housed high-ranking officials. The arrival of a wealthier person was not a big deal. However, this time, Commissioner Lan seemed to have promoted himself for a while. Newspapers from south to north had already reported on it. Local newspapers in Xi'an had naturally reported on it as well. Knowledgeable people felt that he was just a second or third-rate important person and didn't pay much attention. This accountant was still an amateur when it came to officials, and couldn't resist Jie Fu's repeated statements that he was a central government official. Usually, when central government officials came, they stayed at the only luxurious guesthouse in the provincial capital, Xincheng Hotel. This time, a big official came, but he didn't stay at Xincheng Hotel, but at the inn. He was like Bao Zheng on a private visit, coming to investigate the good and bad of the people. It would be better to be more respectful. (291)

Incense Drifting Record

— Originally written by Princess Deling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

Her voice was very low and trembling, probably because she was too happy at the moment. When people are too happy, their hearts often tremble.

"Let's hurry and pick those pale green lotuses," the Empress Dowager said again. "Before we have breakfast, let's put them in a clean vase to offer them before the statue of the Guanyin Bodhisattva. Such rare and wondrous flowers should be offered to the Bodhisattva first!"

The Empress Dowager was very devout in her worship of the Guanyin Bodhisattva, and I myself had a considerable amount of faith. However, at this moment, my mind was still preoccupied with the governor who had been sent to Heilongjiang, so I didn't pay attention to this point. But later, I decided to let go of this troublesome matter and focus on watching the eunuchs who had been ordered by the Empress Dowager to pick lotuses, rowing small boats back and forth in the lotus bushes. The Empress Dowager kept having people shout loudly to guide them. Before we returned to the palace, in addition to the green lotuses offered to the Bodhisattva, several baskets were also filled with ordinary pink lotuses. The Empress Dowager was truly pleased today!

Chapter 32: The Empress Dowager's Dressing Table

Long before Westerners dazzled the world with makeup techniques, our Empress Dowager had long discovered many beauty secrets, some of which have yet to be discovered by others! So I confirmed at that time that every morning before the court, going with the Empress Dowager to her dressing room to watch her slowly and methodically put on makeup was equivalent to taking a "beauty class," and we could always get new experiences, and we would never stand for half a day in vain. Because the old lady was always very careful in the engineering of facial makeup. (391)

Short Story

Rebirth

— Wu Yafei

Suddenly, I received a letter from Ming. He told me that he had arrived in Changsha and was working as a Dean of Discipline in a rural experimental middle school. He said: "Although I have become disillusioned with the education field and am indeed a bit tired of the education profession, I also feel somewhat doubtful about myself. Now I have finally been drawn into the vortex of education again. If it were an ordinary middle school, I might have decided not to do it, but this is a rural experimental middle school, so I am willing to sacrifice my own principles and become a pioneer in rural education..."

Ming is a complete pessimist. When he opens his mouth, it's always with a pessimistic tone, talking about sorrow and worries! He often had them hanging on the corners of his mouth, and it was rare to see a smile on his face. Usually, he would hide at home all day, studying his philosophy of life. Although he and I were classmates and fellow villagers, we were very different in temperament, so we were aloof from each other, but we were more intimate than with other friends.

Although I opposed his pessimism, I understood his pain and sometimes sincerely tried to persuade or comfort him. Even if I couldn't reduce the amount of his sorrow and worries, he could take me as a confidant.

"Fei, you are the only one who knows me in my life! You are my true confidant. There is no one else besides you! Even my parents and siblings cannot understand me!" he often said to me.

"Ming, being a person is just playing in the world, living one day at a time. You should do what you want to do in your heart and not do what you don't want to do. Why are you so serious? You are too hard on yourself! How can there be anything completely satisfactory or anyone completely happy in the world?" I often comforted him like this.

He had attempted suicide three times, but his family managed to save him. I didn't sympathize with him for his suicide, but instead blamed him heavily. Later, he seemed to have realized something, so whenever I went to blame him, he always expressed infinite shame!

"One must be brave, the more one suffers, the stronger one's will becomes, especially a young person. One should not be discouraged but needs to work hard and struggle to remove the obstacles in front of you!"

Indeed, he has changed now. This change has made him a brand new and ambitious young man. He struggled out of the net of his previous depression and created his new life. The reason for his recent change is that he has a lover who understands him better than I do, who is encouraging him and revitalizing his withering soul.

Last month, due to the encouragement of that lover, he left Shanghai and went to Changsha with her to be pioneers in rural education. At the same time, it was the beginning of their pure and happy life.

When I received this good news, how happy I was!

"He is reborn, our Ming's life has a purpose, and the soul of this new person has a home!" I couldn't help but say silently.

Seven Provincial Education Departments Jointly Present to the Central Government: Guaranteeing Temple Property for Education; All Used for Reorganizing Primary Schools

(Changsha, 15th) The Education Departments of Hunan, Zhejiang, Shandong, Anhui, Hubei, Henan, and Jiangsu provinces jointly submitted a petition to the central government, earnestly guaranteeing temple property for education, strictly implementing measures to regulate temples, and using all the funds to reorganize short-term primary schools or other local education undertakings.

Ministry of Education Issues Instructions to National Northeastern University for Earnest Improvement

The Ministry of Education issued instructions on the 15th to National Northeastern University, stating in brief that the university had previously been instructed to comply with the key points for improvement suggested by the ministry. According to reports from inspectors, the university has paid attention to discipline and the students are diligent and hardworking. The teaching in the College of Engineering is conscientious, which is commendable. The university has complied with the previous instructions to reorganize the departments. The points that should be improved in the future are suggested below:

1. The original classes in the Department of Foreign Languages, the Department of Law, and the Department of Education of the university have been terminated and should not be established again. The Departments of History and Geography, the Departments of Political Economy, and the Departments of Chinese and Border Administration should enroll students once every other year. This year, the Departments of History and Geography and Border Administration will enroll students. The Department of Border Administration already has groups studying Japanese and Russian. This year, it can enroll a Russian group at its discretion.

2. Next year, the College of Engineering will only enroll freshmen in the Department of Civil Engineering. The Department of Mechanical and Electrical Engineering will be suspended, but it can set up an Electrical Engineering Specialty at its discretion. The original students in the Department of Mechanical and Electrical Engineering can be sent to other schools for further study or transferred to the Electrical Engineering Specialty at its discretion.

3. There are too many part-time teachers. This should be greatly reduced and replaced with excellent full-time teachers to meet the requirement that part-time teachers should not exceed two-thirds of the total number of teachers. The selection and hiring must be prudent.

4. The university's annual funding is 300,000 yuan. According to the minimum standards set by the ministry, 15% should be used for equipment expenses, i.e., 45,000 yuan per year, plus the special equipment subsidy from the Ministry of Finance of 20,000 yuan per year, totaling 65,000 yuan. This amount should be used for the purchase of books, instruments, and equipment for the colleges.

5. There are too many administrative personnel in the university. This should be strictly reduced to save on expenditures. Matters related to the university's reforms should be submitted to the university affairs and academic affairs meetings for discussion and decision. The above is hereby ordered for compliance and reporting.

Municipal Education Bureau to Examine Academic Performance of Primary and Secondary Schools; Determines Method of Sampling and Review

The Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau issued instructions to public and private primary and secondary schools in the city, stating that in order to examine and urge the earnest improvement of the academic performance of public and private primary and secondary schools in the city, the bureau has formulated the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau's Method for Sampling and Reviewing Academic Performance of Public and Private Primary and Secondary Schools to assess the progress of the academic performance of various primary and secondary schools. The formulated method has been submitted to the municipal government and the Ministry of Education for review and approval. It should be announced for implementation immediately and implemented from this semester. In addition to separate orders, the method is attached for the information of all public and private primary and secondary schools in the city. This order includes the Method for Sampling and Reviewing Academic Performance of Public and Private Primary and Secondary Schools issued by the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau. Article 1: In order to examine the academic performance of various primary and secondary schools in the city and urge earnest improvement, the bureau, in addition to carrying out inspections and guidance, has formulated this method to assess their progress. Article 2: The bureau may notify the schools by telephone or special messenger to sample and review the following types of achievements of various primary and secondary schools in the city: (1) Students' exam papers; (2) Students' exercise books; (3) Students' notes and reports; (4) Students' diaries; (5) Students' review records; (6) Trial teaching plans. Article 3: After receiving a telephone or special messenger notification from the bureau to sample various achievements, the various primary and secondary schools in the city should send the sampled achievements to the bureau within 24 hours by special messenger, relying on the receipt issued by the bureau as the time for assessing the schools' submission of achievements to the bureau. Article 4: The bureau will review the achievements sent by the various primary and secondary schools within three days and publish the awards and punishments in the bureau's Education Weekly. During the review period, the primary and secondary schools should prepare a copy for application. Article 5: The achievements sampled as stipulated in Article 1 of this method refer to all achievements of a certain subject and grade (including practical achievements), and also include all tables related to the achievements of the subject. Article 6: The achievements submitted by the various primary and secondary schools should include all achievements from the beginning of this semester to the date of sampling, unless the bureau has specified a period. When a certain subject achievement is specified for sampling, a list of all students in the grade, the name of the teacher of the subject, the textbooks used, and whether students have taken leave of absence should be attached. Article 7: The academic achievements submitted by the various primary and secondary schools should be marked with the date and item of the assignment by the students, and the responsible teachers should sign and mark the date of review on a regular basis. Article 8: This method shall be implemented from the date it is submitted to the municipal government and the Ministry of Education for the record.

Certification Examination for Secondary and Normal School Teachers; Oral Exams to Begin Tomorrow; Subject Exams to Conclude Today; Ministry of Education Clarifies Doubts Regarding Educational Experience

The certification examination for secondary and normal school teachers, organized by the Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau, has been held at Aurora University since the 12th of this month. Written examinations will be completed today, and oral examinations will be held tomorrow morning and afternoon, also at Aurora University. After the oral examinations, the entire process will be concluded. Furthermore, the Education Bureau, due to doubts regarding educational experience in Articles 4 and 5 of the Regulations for Certification Examinations for Secondary and Normal School Teachers, submitted a request for clarification to the Ministry of Education. It is now understood that the Ministry of Education has replied, stating that for those who have graduated from schools above the specialized subject level, their educational experience is not limited to any particular level of school. However, the educational experience of those who have graduated from schools equivalent to the senior high school level should be limited to secondary schools.

Boy Scout Council Meeting Held Yesterday

The Shanghai Boy Scout Council held its 25th council meeting yesterday. Council members present were Pan Gongzhan (represented by Du Gang), Leng Xueqiao, Qu Yue, Luo Lie, Shen Yu, Sun Yiming, Zhao Weizu, Yu Kuiyuan, Jin Xing, Sun Yixin, and Xi Yutong, among others. The meeting was chaired by Qu Yue, with Xie Yanbo as the recorder. Formalities were observed. A. Reporting Matters: (1) The General Association instructed that the work report for this semester and the outline of the work plan for the next semester should be submitted for review within August of this year. (2) The General Association instructed all regions to open Boy Scout training classes and file records in accordance with regulations. (3) The General Association instructed that the National Boy Scout Disaster Relief Mobilization Regulations be issued and forwarded to all groups for compliance. (4) Greetings to representatives passing through on their way to the United States, with the rest omitted. B. Matters for Discussion: (1) The Standing Committee suggested that due to the hot weather during the summer vacation, the working hours of the council should be changed to 8:00 AM to 12:00 PM. (Decision) Approved retroactively. (2) The Standing Committee suggested that council meetings be held irregularly during the summer vacation. (Decision) Approved retroactively. (3) Proposal to formulate a work plan for the second year. (Decision) The Standing Committee and the Secretary will draft it and all departments will provide input. (4) Council Member Qu Yue's letter of resignation due to leaving Shanghai. (Decision) Approved. The vacant council member position will be filled by alternate council member Shen Yu in accordance with the law. (5) The term of office of the Standing Committee members of this council has expired. Re-election will be conducted in accordance with the general charter. (Decision) Council members Tong Xingbai, Pan Gongzhan, and Leng Xueqiao will serve. (6) The East Asia Radio Training School has revised the date for the graduation ceremony. A request has been made for a representative to attend and provide guidance. (Decision) Secretary Luo will attend. (7) How should the Boy Scout general mobilization for disaster relief work be managed? (Decision) Council Member Shen Yu will draft a plan and submit it to the next standing committee meeting. The meeting adjourned.

Quanzhou People's Livelihood Agricultural School Delegation Walks Through North China, Returns to Shanghai Yesterday, Walking Over 2,500 Li Through Dozens of Counties

The North China Agricultural Education Visiting Group of the Fujian Quanzhou Zisheng Agricultural School, following in the footsteps of last year's China Coastal Walking Group, conducted a walking tour of North China. They arrived in Shanghai on the 1st of last month from Quanzhou, visiting the Gongxue Tuan, Nian Er She, Huangdu Rural Teachers' School, and Lida Agricultural Science Education Center, among other places. Later, they took a boat to Qingdao. It is understood that after the delegation arrived in Qingdao, they were led by the municipal government to visit municipal construction projects, etc. They then left Qingdao and walked along the Jiaoji Railway, passing through Chengyang, Jiaozhou, Gaomi, Zeshan Tanxian, Changle, Yidu, Zouping, Longshan, and Jinan counties, examining civil education, free education, and rural enterprises along the way. Chairman Han of the provincial government telegraphed the counties to provide protection, so the delegation's journey was very convenient. They also followed the Jinpu Railway to Dezhou, Jingxian in Hebei, Fucheng, Wuqiang, Raoyang, Anping, Boye, and Dingxian counties, and then along the Banhan Line to Baoding. In all the places they visited, they toured various construction projects and other social education organizations and groups. After arriving in Beiping, they visited the municipal government, the Bureau of Social Affairs, the Yanjing University Qinghe Experimental Zone, the China International Famine Relief Commission, the Agricultural Experiment Field, the Family Welfare Association, and the School for the Deaf and Dumb, among other places. They also toured ancient palaces and parks. Then, they walked to the top of the Juyongguan and Badaling Great Walls, gazing out at the area beyond the pass with deep emotion. After walking back to Tianjin, they took a boat and returned to Shanghai yesterday. It is estimated that the delegation traveled by boat and ship for more than two months, walking through dozens of counties, covering more than 2,900 li, and gaining a wealth of knowledge from their visits. It was truly a grand undertaking. They will prepare a detailed report after returning to Quanzhou, it is said.

Zhang Taiyan to Lecture in Suzhou; Lectures to Begin on September 16th

Yu Hang Zhang Taiyan, a master of classical learning, has been enjoying himself writing books since he settled in Suzhou. This spring, the National Government sent him 10,000 yuan to show respect for the elderly. Zhang used the funds to prepare for a lecture series, building a lecture hall, providing seating, and inviting scholars from all directions to come to Suzhou to listen to the lectures and reside in the meeting hall. It is understood that the preparations for the meeting have been completed, and all lecture halls, dormitories, and lounges have been completed. The lecture classes set up during the summer vacation have also ended. From September 16th, a formal and large-scale lecture series will begin. Scholars from other provinces are being sought to register. The charter will be sent upon request. The address of the meeting is No. 50 Jinfan Road, Suzhou City. It is said that scholars from various places, even from remote provinces, are registering in an endless stream. In the future, the revival of national studies and the flourishing of culture will depend on this one line of hope. It is also heard that from September onwards, the association will publish a bi-monthly journal called "Zhi Yan," which will focus on elucidating national studies. The content will be classified, provisionally including categories such as "General Theory," "Special Studies," "Glossary," "Women's Garden," "Special Records," and "Miscellaneous Records." If there are unpublished works by predecessors, they can be submitted to the publication for special publication. It has been decided that Mr. Taiyan will be the chief editor, and his disciples Sun Yingruo, Ge Yufu, Jin Donglei, Wang Peizheng, Zhu Zegeng, Wang Chenglu, Pan Jingzheng, and Wu Deyi will serve as members of the board of directors, responsible for editing, publishing, and other matters. The special writers are all famous figures in the country, including Huang Jigang, Shao Tanqiu, Qian Xuantong, and Wang Xuchu, among dozens of others. Furthermore, the lecture notes from Mr. Zhang's weekly lectures in the first half of the year have been published up to the sixth volume, priced at two jiao per volume, and will be sent upon request.

Reorganization of Shanghai County Middle School; Former Principal Fan Chongheng Not Removed from Office

A letter from the Shanghai County Education Bureau stated, "Dear Sirs, Today's education news column in your newspaper published an item on the county-run junior middle school, with the headline 'County-Run Junior Middle School Principal Removed from Office and Another Appointed.' Although the school is being reorganized according to the Education Department's order, there is no mention of removing the former principal, Fan Chongheng, from office. Moreover, the report issued by the provincial supervisor stated that 'administrative facilities are extremely serious.' The reorganization was only carried out because the graduation examination results of the students taking the provincial examination this year were relatively poor. It was not a suspension. We respectfully request that you make a correction to avoid causing confusion. Sincerely, Shanghai County Education Bureau, August 15, 24th year."

Alumni of Liangjiang School to Meet Today; at Zhengxing Girls' Middle School on Seymour Road

The Liangjiang Women's Physical Education Normal School in this city has been established for 15 years, with a total of 18 classes of graduates, numbering nearly a thousand people. Their origins are scattered throughout the provinces and cities of the country. Most of them serve at home and abroad, and their achievements have long been known to society. The school's reputation has grown in recent years due to its progress in construction and its efforts in promoting practical education. This year marks the 15th anniversary, and the alumni attach great importance to the school's hard work and difficult management over the years. A grand celebration is planned. A meeting will be held first in Shanghai by various schools, and then the entire group will be gradually contacted to carry out preparations. Huang Daping, the principal of Zhengxing Girls' Middle School, and Jiang Lixian of Great China University, both alumni of the school, have initiated and convened a meeting of alumni in Shanghai, scheduled for 3:00 PM today in the auditorium of Zhengxing Girls' Middle School on Seymour Road. The agenda for discussion will be divided into two main parts: (1) How to gather other graduates and carry out preparatory work for a grand celebration to mark the 15th anniversary of the school this winter. (2) How should the graduates maintain close contact with each other and discuss ways to contribute to the development of women's physical education? All will be discussed.

American Legal Scholar Dr. Pound Arrives in Shanghai

Dr. Pound, the world-renowned legal scholar and dean of the Harvard University Law School, arrived in Shanghai yesterday morning on the President Lincoln. Accompanying him was Dr. Yang Yongqing, president of the University of the Pacific, who was returning from lecturing in Honolulu. Dr. Pound is a leading figure in the modern sociological jurisprudence school, and his writings are extensive. Many European universities use them as teaching materials. His legal thought has greatly influenced the improvement of laws in various countries around the world and can be called the leader of the legal community in the twentieth century. He has recently been invited by Dr. Wu Jingxiong, dean of the Soochow Law School, to visit China. At the same time, he will assist Dr. Wu in designing the organization and curriculum of the Soochow Law School's graduate school. He will stay in Shanghai for about three or four days. It is heard that the Soochow Law School Alumni Association, the Harvard Alumni Association, and the Shanghai Bar Association are preparing a welcome.

Spanish Professor Arrives in Shanghai for Investigation

The Dalu News reports that Professor Garcia, from the University of Barcelona in Spain, along with forty colleagues, is traveling to the East to investigate the culture that Spain once spread to the world, and its current remaining influence. They arrived in Shanghai from Manila on Wednesday. The professor and his colleagues traveled to South America, Central America, Mexico, and Cuba last year, and spent some days at several famous universities in the United States. They achieved excellent results last year, so this year they came to the Far East to continue their exploration. After completing their public affairs, they will set off to return to Marseille.

Sports News

Final Performance Measurement at Qingdao Training Camp; National Records in 100 Meters and Discus; 100 Meters in 10.6 Seconds, Discus in 37.92 Meters; 16.2 Seconds in High Hurdles Ties National Record; Training Camp and Lecture Series Conclude Simultaneously

(Qingdao, 15th Dispatch) The training camp conducted its final performance measurement at the sports field at 9:00 AM on the 15th. All events were measured except for the 10,000 meters, 800 meters, and long jump. The results were mostly excellent. Liu Changchun ran the 100 meters in 10.6 seconds, breaking the national average for the Far East Games. Dai Shuguo ran the 400 meters in 52.8 seconds, exceeding the set standard. Lin Shaozhou ran the high hurdles in 16.2 seconds, restoring his own record from the National Games. Chen Baoqiu threw the discus 37.92 meters, breaking the national record previously held by Leng Peigen. Yang Daogui achieved 14.15 meters in the triple jump, exceeding the standard. The teaching staff, students, and athletes from both the lecture series and the training camp will leave Qingdao separately within a few days.

(Qingdao, Central News Agency, 15th) The charity basketball game of the summer training camp was held at 4:00 PM on the 15th. Players from the training camp all took the field to perform. The lecture series examination was completed at noon on the 15th. Both events concluded simultaneously on the evening of the 15th, but without ceremony.

The competition will be hosted by the International Educational Film Association and will be held in Berlin from September 10th to 20th of this year. Little Men (16)

— Original work by Ms. Louisa May Alcott, translated by Zheng Xiaocang (Zonghai)

Pomponio was the leader of the attacking party, and Nat defended his chamber with a bravery and persistence worthy of all praise. He picked up the cushions as fast as they were thrown, till the besiegers’ ammunition was all gone; then they rallied for a final assault, to recover their lost arms. Some slight bruises were given and received, but no one minded, and every one took and gave resounding whacks with perfect good nature, while the pillows flew like snowflakes, till Mrs. Jo, looking at her watch, cried out,—

“Time’s up, boys! Into bed, great and small, or there’ll be a penalty.”

“What penalty?” asked Ned, sitting up, eager to know what would be done to any daring spirit who defied this most singular and philanthropic of schoolmistresses.

“No play next time,” answered Mrs. Jo. “I give them five minutes to settle down, then the lights go out, and order must be restored. They are boys of honor, and they will keep their word.”

Which, indeed, they did. For the cessation of hostilities was as sudden as the beginning,—a farewell fling, a final cheer,—as Nat launched a seventh cushion at the retreating foe,—a few boasts about what they would do next time, and then order was perfectly restored; only a few chuckles and whispers broke the silence which followed the uproar, as Mrs. Jo kissed her new boarder, and left him to dream all sorts of happy dreams of Plumfield life.

Numbering notes for this article, which is printed daily. The 14th should have been (14), but was mistakenly (13). The 15th should have been (15), but was mistakenly (14). This is corrected here.

Commercial News

Finance: Rumors of US Purchasing Large Amounts of Silver, Gold Market Suddenly Collapses, Heavy Selling Pressure Surrounds, Bank Notes Plunge, Breaks Through Four Major Levels, Plunges to 18.2 Yuan

The gold market overseas experienced a sharp contraction yesterday due to rumors of the US halting silver purchases. However, major players in the market had already become suspicious. Indeed, after the market opened, news refuting the US Treasury Secretary's statement spread, causing gold prices to plummet repeatedly and struggle to recover. At the beginning of the morning, overseas silver markets in both the UK and the US reported sharp declines. However, market players stated that the market had continued to decline by 0.25 after closing and that the US had purchased silver at that price. The forward silver price in Montreux plunged by 1.52 to 1.72. Exchange rates generally increased. Spot gold in London contracted by 1.5 pence. In off-market pre-market trading, bids were called at 25.56 yuan, but there were no transactions. Chunyuan, Yongfuxing, Yongda, Fayongheng, Yu Dachangxiang, and Dada all sold. The price immediately dropped from 22 yuan to 19 yuan. This was due to the Reuters London silver market report, which stated that the US had aggressively purchased over 15 million ounces of silver during the sharp decline. The general psychology was that the report of the US stopping silver purchases was unfounded, fueling the fear of selling. However, although Shenfeng, Wanxing, Yongli, Huixiang, and others were still buying at lower prices, Yongchang, Yuanmao, Yongyuqing, Yongfuyu, Hengchang, and Yongheng were still selling, causing the price to fall to 17.18 yuan. After the market opened, the Central Bank's listing was announced, with both the UK and the US remaining unchanged. Customs gold units contracted by 0.03 yuan. The benchmark price for Standard Gold was reduced to 930.6 yuan, making it difficult to recover. Major players such as Hengchang, Yongfuxing, Yongfuyu, Yuanmao, and Yongchunyuan aggressively sold, causing the price to fall sharply. A Reuters report stated that the US Treasury Secretary announced that the amount of silver purchased today had exceeded 25 million ounces, indicating that the silver purchasing program would continue. Additionally, Thomas advocated for a thorough investigation into the silver purchasing program. The price then retreated into the 10 yuan range. Despite some fluctuations, the exchange market remained surprisingly tight. Bank notes were aggressively sold again. In addition, an Associated Press report stated that the US Treasury Secretary dismissed the rumors of stopping silver purchases as unfounded and said that the amount of silver coin coupons currently in circulation exceeded the silver reserves by a significant amount, and the government should continue to purchase enough silver. This further fueled the selling pressure, causing the price to break through the 900 yuan level again. Soon after, it retreated into the 890 yuan range. Banks continued to seek settlements. It was also reported that the Central Bank had started spot trading, and buyers were actively purchasing at lower prices, causing the selling pressure to subside slightly and the price to recover by about 8 yuan. Banks took advantage of the high prices to sell, but there was still congestion from the mainland. The predicted price increase for Indian silver was twelve annas, but the price increase was hindered. The afternoon trend weakened again. In the afternoon market, the forward premium fell after the sellers offered a half-yuan discount, causing sentiment to improve slightly and the price to rise to above 5 yuan. The Indian silver price was reported to have risen by nineteen annas, triggering a reversal. After the opening, the price was flat. HSBC sought some settlements. The market was weak but stabilized, and the forward premium gradually decreased. There were several attempts to pull up the price, but market sentiment remained depressed. After that, the price fluctuated intermittently without any significant changes. In the end, the market lacked support. In the afternoon, Reuters re-reported the negative news, causing a sudden drop in price and pushing it back into the 90-yuan range. The situation became more precarious. Banks continued to seek settlements. The market closed flat and stabilized. After the market closed, the Indian silver price was soft but stable. This session’s forward market saw the short side offer a discount of 1.3 yuan to 0.8 yuan. The day’s market conditions are recorded below.

The morning opening was 917 yuan, which was a slight increase of 0.3 yuan compared to the previous closing. However, it was significantly lower than the post-closing and evening dark trading prices. Fuyu, Fuxing, Yongda, Fayong, Chunyuan, and Yongjin still rose to 8 yuan. The Central Bank's listing was announced, with customs gold units contracting by 0.03 yuan. Hengyu, Fu and Yong, Huixiang, Yuanchang, Yonghengchang, and Yong Yongli Dadesheng Yisheng sold notes, causing the price to fall to 4.8 yuan. Huabi bought September US dollars at 0.0625. Page 17

Free Talk

Court Art and Reality

— Qu Yi

Recently, I saw a collotype edition of the Geng Zhi Tu (耕織圖, "Illustrations of Agriculture and Sericulture") from the Kangxi imperial collection. It was painted by Jiao Bingzhen, an official of the Qin Tian Jian (欽天監, Imperial Astronomical Observatory). The entire book contains twenty-three agricultural paintings and twenty-three sericultural paintings. At the beginning of the book, there is a title page by Luo Zhenyu. And a five-page preface to the Illustrations of Agriculture and Sericulture by the emperor. According to the opinion of Emperor Kangxi, who wrote the preface, he ordered the Qin Tian Jian to paint forty-six paintings for him to look at, which he also called one of his ways of governing. His preface says:

"I have been diligent day and night, studying governance, and thinking that the foundation of the people is food and clothing. I have often read the poems of Bin Feng and Wu Yi, which are complete with descriptions of farming and sericulture. In the past, people used them to be played on instruments and made into canonizations. Those who have the world and the country must repeatedly consider them. The edicts of the Western Han Dynasty were the closest to ancient times, and they said: 'If farming is harmed, it is the root of starvation; if women's work is harmed, it is the source of cold.' It also says, 'The elderly can end their lives with longevity, and the young orphans can grow up.' Those who want to achieve this goal must focus on the fundamentals. Every time I inspect the customs and folk songs, I happily observe agricultural affairs. I know very clearly the nature of the soil in the north and south, the suitability of planting millet and sorghum, the differences in seasons, and the methods of capturing and treating locusts. When I listen to politics, I always talk about it with the officials. On the side of Fengjin Garden, I have cultivated several fields, surrounded by streams. The fields are well-arranged, and the sound of water wheels fills my ears. Every year, I harvest thousands of bundles of good crops. I plant mulberry trees by the fields and set up silkworm sheds. The cocoons are reeled into silk, and it is as if I am next door to a thatched cottage. Therefore, I built the Zhi Jia Xuan and Qiu Yun Zhai to observe them. The ancients said, 'When wearing silk, think of the cold of the weaving girls; when eating grain, think of the suffering of the farmers.' I am deeply concerned about this. Therefore, I painted twenty-three agricultural paintings and twenty-three sericultural paintings. I wrote a poem for each painting to show the hard work, and presented them in the paintings. From the beginning to the end, the hard work of the farmers and the exhaustion of the silkworm girls are all shown in detail. I have ordered them to be engraved and circulated to let my descendants and subjects know that grain is hard to come by and clothing is not easy to get..."

This preface can be said to be extremely well-written. That's why I copied a large section of it. What makes us most concerned about is that he can cultivate a few acres of land, plant a few mulberry trees, build some silkworm sheds, and personally observe farming and sericulture to show his concern for agricultural affairs. However, in each of the forty-six paintings, the setting and the arrangement of the characters are extremely detailed and delicate. The twenty-three agricultural paintings are: soaking seeds, plowing, harrowing, cultivating, rolling, transplanting seedlings, first seedlings, silting, pulling seedlings, transplanting seedlings, first weeding, second weeding, third weeding, irrigating, harvesting, threshing, holding ears of grain, spring pestle, threshing, winnowing, grinding, storing, and offering sacrifices to the gods. The twenty-three sericultural paintings are: bathing silkworms, second sleep, third sleep, great rising, catching spinners, dividing the cocoon frames, picking mulberries, placing on cocoon frames, roasting cocoon frames, removing from cocoon frames, selecting cocoons, storing cocoons, reeling silk, silkworm moths, offering sacrifices, weft, weaving, winding silk, warp, dyeing, picking flowers, cutting silk, and making clothes. Although the production process of these agricultural and sericultural affairs is correct, the depiction of each painting is too beautified. The countryside is painted as a poetic realm, secluded and beautiful. Similarly, just talking about the agricultural paintings, every farmer is weak and soft, with a plump face and clear eyebrows, completely like an elegant gentleman. For example, in the painting of transplanting seedlings, two farmers each carry a basket, smiling and talking while slowly scattering the seeds in their hands like feeding chickens, as if there is infinite work pleasure. This is undoubtedly a distortion of reality. As far as I have seen, when farmers transplant seedlings, they sow with force, scattering the seeds on a field surface by field surface. There is definitely no such leisure and ease of scattering and talking. However, it is precisely because of this leisure and ease that it is suitable for the emperor's eyes. Otherwise, if the author really painted a rough and hard-working farmer scattering grain, it might make the emperor unhappy.

Also, such as during the third weeding and irrigation, it is the hottest weather. Most of the farmers in the countryside work shirtless. But here, everyone is still neatly dressed, and there is not a single naked person. Nakedness would naturally be offensive to the emperor's eyes. Although it is the truth, it must still be concealed. Being able to conceal it allows the emperor to be happy, to develop poetic inspiration, and to write a poem for each painting. Although the poems are extremely clumsy, the emperor's happiness is obvious. Look at the poem he wrote for the first seedling painting:

"Spring work is just in time, look at the schedule for planting seeds; take the time to take your children out, leaning on a cane to the road; watch the flood in West Lake, face the wind in the late afternoon; the farmer's affairs are knowable, should take countless efforts." Here, although the last sentence mentions the hard work of farming, the whole poem paints the happy situation of the farmers—and the emperor seems to share a joy in this happiness.

In fact, in these twenty-three agricultural paintings, there is not one that is not filled with happiness and harmonious emotion—the landlord's kindness to the farmers, the intimacy between the farmers, and the joy of the mothers and children, all feel that this day is peaceful and happy.—What a truly peaceful and happy countryside! Thus, the world is also prosperous, and the ability of art to serve as an ornament of prosperity is also exhausted.

But reality does not allow the author to excessively conceal the truth. Artworks should be the results of truly experiencing from real life to be great. If artworks are used as one of the services of the court and used to decorate peace, then the author's thoughts and feelings must be based on the thoughts and feelings of the master in the court. Reality is just borrowing some materials to use. Therefore, a contradiction between content and form arises. For example, here, the rough life content of the countryside is expressed as a graceful and gentle style, separating art from reality. Although the emperor is quite enlightened after seeing it, if the farmers themselves come to see it, they may suspect that this is another world and another human affair.

Journey in the Gorge (Continued)

— Fang Wu

I then told him that this was something that could not be avoided, because when walking in those mountains, if you didn't claim to be doing business, others wouldn't be willing to walk with you, and they wouldn't be happy to talk to you.

"Then, what exactly are you doing?"

"Me, my stomach is forcing me to walk, as long as I can survive, I will do it!

"Oh!"

That man then tilted his head and smiled sarcastically at my traveling companion.

"You've simply been deceived! ... What kind of person do you think you can deceive? Go home and watch your cow!"

My traveling companion sat down dejectedly on the ground, not saying a word, not answering, just puffing on his dry tobacco pipe with a creaking sound.

At this time, I felt that my danger had passed, and I could freely walk my way. But the man suddenly slapped his thigh and shouted at me:

"Good fellow, you have the ability to deceive him, then come with us: you are willing to do anything."

Then, suddenly remembering something, he grabbed my shoulder, shook it hard, squinted his right eye, and widened his left eye, staring at me as if he wanted to see through my lungs, and asked loudly:

"How did you get out? Tell me, tell me honestly! Did you injure the master's family with a hoe like him (pointing at my traveling companion)?... Tell me, you have to tell me honestly!"

I shook my head and said I was not like that. He raised his eyebrows, showing a thoughtful expression, and muttered to himself in a low voice:

"Hmm, it's a bird that still has a nest."

Then he showed a decisive and flexible appearance, waved his hand at me, and said humorously to me:

"Friend, go your way, I wish you good luck and make a fortune all the way!"

At this time, I breathed a sigh of relief, as if I had just emerged from the water. When I walked forward a dozen or twenty steps with my baggage, the man suddenly shouted loudly from behind:

"Hey, come back! Come back!"

I was surprised, but I had to follow him back.

With a worried heart for his arrangements, I walked to his front. He was already sitting cross-legged on a large stone, with a half-smoked cigarette hanging from the corner of his mouth, still showing the same leisurely and contented expression as before. He pointed his finger at the opposite side of him and said with a sarcastic smile:

"Don't be afraid, sit down..., you just met, now you should be old friends."

I couldn't help but sit down, but the baggage was still on my back.

"Throw away your rotten baggage! ... Hmm, it's so precious, there must be a little bit..."

I had to take it off, and my heart couldn't help but jump, thinking:

"What is this guy going to do!"

At the same time, I secretly glanced at the villager. He was bending over, reaching into the grass under the Forsythia, reaching out his wrist and touching something.

The man in front of me had already taken the cigarette from his mouth and threw it into the river, showing an impatient look, and urged me repeatedly.

"Hurry up, hurry up,... you are always so slow!"

I was a little sweaty.

Soon, the thing was taken out, which was a baggage. The man grabbed it and quickly opened it. The aroma of dried beef and dry wheat cakes immediately rose. While shouting "Eat", he tore a piece of dried beef and stuffed it into his mouth.

I hesitated. The villager squatted beside me and devoured it, as if he hadn't eaten yesterday.

"Eat, what are you doing stupidly? ... Are you a fool?"

The man stuffed a piece of beef into my hand, and when he saw that I didn't dare to accept it, he said sincerely:

"Aren't you hungry? Eat!"

My face turned red, and I stuttered:

"Don't... don't joke with me, I can't afford this meal."

"Nonsense, don't be so stupid! If you can afford it, I won't let you eat it!"

The man said with a slightly angry look, pulling out the tendon stuck in his teeth and throwing it into the river.

When he was full, the man smiled at me and said:

"Old friend, you can leave now! We are going too!"

Then he solemnly instructed:

"Keep walking straight, but don't look back!... You know, we mean what we say!"

I understood the rules of these people, words are law. Really, I walked around the hillside without looking back.

The sound of the river roared all the way, constantly spitting out white foam, as if a group of naughty elementary school students had been released from strict schools and were laughing madly.

The kingfisher quickly skimmed over the water, sometimes approaching the side of the road I was walking on, and sometimes flying far away. Wild ducks flapped their brown wings and called happily, flying up in groups of three or five, and then floating on the water in groups of three or five to chase each other.

The forsythia with small yellow flowers and the branches and leaves of some ash trees swayed happily in the river breeze, fluttering.

I took a deep breath of the fresh air in the gorge, blowing a whistle and walking happily.

Lodging

— Shi Dai

— One of the Small Scenes of Qidong Mountain Wilds —

The setting sun blushingly reddened its face, hiding towards the western slope of Hugou Mountain. Bathed in the light of the evening sun, the verdant mountain peaks appeared especially tranquil and lush. The densely leaved oaks soared high above the pine forest, craning their necks to gaze at the evening glow on the horizon. Their slender shadows silently massaged the pine branches. The pine branches darkened, the blurred light landing on the mound-like stone mounds, gradually fading in color.

From the distant valley came bursts of pastoral thunder, momentarily drowned out by the evening chanting of the monks.

"Let's rest a while before moving on! I'm really exhausted!"

"It's almost dark. Why don't we just walk to the temple halfway up the mountain and rest there? Maybe it's the Niangniang Temple?" Sister Shan pointed to the temple halfway up the mountain to the west.

"That's right, we can even find lodging there!"

Fatigue burned fiercely, and with the last remnants of our strength, we managed to round the Jiao Lv Ridge and cross a deep valley. The rugged mountain path lay prostrate beneath our feet, and we would accidentally stub our toes on a rock or stumble over a stone. Sister Xuan kept grumbling, complaining, "Why didn't we hire mules to ride in Shiliu Chuang?" But Sister Shan and I endured in silence.

By the time we reached the stone base in front of the temple to sit down, dusk was already drawing in its faint shadows. I ran to the front of the temple and looked up at the red lacquered plaque with golden characters. It really was the "Niangniang Temple." Joy bloomed like a night-blooming cereus, its petals bursting open all at once. I shouted from afar:

"It really is the Niangniang Temple!"

As if fatigue feared joy, my legs felt as light as chicken feathers, and I ran to the stone base like a gust of wind. I patted Sister Xuan on the shoulder:

"We don't have to worry about finding a place to stay."

I was about to knock on the temple door, but Sister Shan said not to rush. "Let's rest first before calling at the door. Anyway, the nun won't refuse us lodging after she sees Third Aunt's letter!" We rested with single-minded determination. Sister Xuan emptied the sand from her shoes, while I was drawn to a small red notice on the stone base. I leaned closer to take a closer look. It read:

"Oh Heavenly Emperor, Oh Earthly Emperor, my family has a crying night lad,

Travelers, gentlemen, recite three times, sleep soundly until dawn."

Night concealed dusk, and the summer heat also plunged into the dark trap along with the mountains. The murmuring stream at the bottom of the Stone Woman River, like a widow's midnight sighs, sliced through the silence of the air and drifted into the valley. Grasshoppers clicked their wings busily in the deep grass, as if deliberately scaring us girls on an adventurous journey.

"A-Dai! Go call at the door!"

The three sisters walked to the temple steps together. I used Sister Xuan's walking stick to knock on the door. The dog inside barked madly and ran over, its paws scratching at the threshold as it bit fiercely. Then someone scolded the dog. The roaring dog stopped barking, and the door opened to reveal a nun in a black robe. Her glowing face wore a look of surprise, her eyes sharply sizing up the three of us sisters.

"Master! Is there a Master Yi here?"

"Ah! Ah..."

She hesitated, clearly suspicious of our origins.

Seeing her like that, I couldn't help but lose my temper:

"We're not bandits or thieves, don't worry. The three of us sisters are from Jiangnan, and we're all students. Please tell us, is Master Yi here or not? If you don't believe us, we have a letter of introduction!"

Why do straightforward people always have to be so blunt? Sister tried to signal me with her eyes, not letting me say anything further.

The old nun finally nodded and let us in.

Darkness enveloped the temple courtyard. Everything was blurry. The dog, with its shining eyes, was barking in the corner. The meditation room was quiet, the faint light of the lamp flickering dimly. The bodhisattva paintings on the wall were almost forgotten by the light.

Sister Xuan opened her leather bag and handed Third Aunt's handwritten letter to the old nun. As soon as she saw the handwriting and signature on the envelope, she knew it was a letter from her old friend Shi Keyun, whom she had known for twenty years. While tearing open the letter, she said to us with a smile:

"I am Jingyi. How is Sister Keyun doing?"

"Thanks to the Master's blessing, Third Aunt is safe and well."

After reading Third Aunt's letter, she entertained us with a smiling face. She went into the inner room and woke up a sleeping little nun, instructing her to start a fire, boil water, and cook rice.

Even though fatigue was fermenting in our bodies, it was impossible to lie down and rest. Master Yi asked us many questions, and the three sisters had to answer them carefully. When we spoke about Third Aunt's life story, she sighed about her own past. Becoming a nun was not her wish. She was not a pessimist, nor was she escaping reality. It was merely a temporary way to settle down. Although she was now the abbess of the Niangniang Temple, this kind of lonely life did not arouse her interest at all.

By the time we finished eating, the night was even quieter. The mountain gate was locked tightly, and the waterfall in the distant mountain stream crashed against the stream, urging us to sleep early. When we lay down at the time, Master Yi was still hunched over the lamp reading the letter we brought.

The Tragedy by the Sea (5)

— Original by French Balzac, translated by Wang Jiansheng

"You know, I will always remember all this, and Chabrame will naturally remember it too," he said after a pause.

"When Jaques Chabrame was fifteen or sixteen years old, he was already a complete little swindler. He often went out to fool people, and waited in the areas of Gironde and Saffran. Then he needed money, so he went to steal from his mother, who didn't dare to utter a word in front of her husband. Labrame was an honest man, and if someone wrote two extra 'sous' on a check, he would have to travel twenty miles to return the money in full."

"Finally, one day when his father was out fishing, his mother was robbed of all her possessions. Their son took the dressing table, pottery, bed sheets, shirts, leaving her nothing but the bare walls. After selling everything he had swept away, he went alone to Nantes to drink. The poor woman cried day and night over this. When his father returned, she wanted to tell him, but she feared the child's father—not for herself—you understand! When Pierre Chabrame returned, he saw his wife's borrowed furniture and said, 'What's going on?' His poor wife was barely alive. Finally, she said, 'We have been robbed!' 'Where did Jaques go?' 'Jaques went drinking alone!' No one knew where this worthless treasure had fled to. 'He really likes to be dissolute!' Pierre said.

"Six months later, the poor father heard that his son was going to be brought to Nantes for trial. He walked there (walking was closer than going by sea) found his son, and brought him back. He didn't ask him, 'What crimes have you committed?' He simply said, 'If you can't live with your mother and me for two years, behave properly, go out fishing for a living, and be an honest man, you'll see what I'll do!' This madman thought his parents were stupid and mocked his father. So Pierre struck him hard on the head, causing Jaques to lie down for six months, while the poor mother withered away with grief.

'One night, as she lay sleeping beside her husband, she heard a clamor. She got out of bed and was stabbed in the arm. She cried out, and they lit a fire. Pierre Chabrame knew his wife was injured. He was convinced it was a robber—as if there really were robbers in this place. Ah, you could carry ten thousand francs with you from Croisic to Saint-Nazaire without worrying about anyone asking you what you were carrying. Pierre went to look for Jaques, but he couldn't find him anywhere. The next morning, the little robber brazenly returned, saying he was living in Batteuse. I should tell you that his mother didn't know where to deposit her money. Chabrame deposited his money with Mr. Le Peule at Croisic. Their son's mischief cost them many pounds, and they were already half ruined, because it was difficult for a person with twelve thousand livres (French silver coins) to spend freely. No one knew how much money Chabrame spent in Nantes to redeem his son. The whole family was trapped in an evil fate. Chabrame's brother also suffered misfortune and sought help. To comfort him, Pierre told him that Jaques should marry Pierrot (Pierrot was Chabrame's brother's daughter) and thus help him make a living. He hired him when he was fishing. Joseph Chabrame also had to work hard for the sake of bread. His wife had died of fever, so she had to pay Pierrot several months' wages for weaning. Pierre Chabrame's wife owed more than a hundred francs to people for soothing the child and for his clothes, and she also owed Dafroux two or three months' wages for bringing milk for Pierrot. Dafroux had a child with Sigodel. Chabrame's wife sewed a Spanish gold coin into the wool of her bedding with the inscription "For Pierrot." He had received a good education. Her handwriting was as neat as a clerk's. She had taught her son to read, and it was this that ruined her family. No one knew about this, but everyone knew that the worthless Jaques had stolen the gold and taken it to Croisic to squander."
