Special Telegraph Edition

Voice of the Telegraph Industry

Administrative Yuan's Order to Government and Military Organs to Pay Telegraph and Telephone Fees

— Zhen

Recently, the Administrative Yuan noted that government, military, and police organs often delayed paying telegraph and telephone fees. When new administrations took over from old ones, new officials often made excuses and refused to pay the outstanding fees from the previous administration's tenure. As a result, telegraph revenue has been steadily decreasing. The Yuan has therefore issued a special order to all ministries, commissions, provincial and municipal governments, and their affiliated organs, stating that all telegraph and telephone fees must be paid monthly. In cases of changeover, outgoing and incoming officials must not make excuses and pass the buck. Otherwise, telegraph and telephone services will be suspended in accordance with the regulations of the telegraph and telephone bureaus. This is the most effective order issued by the Administrative Yuan at the request of the Ministry of Communications to rectify outstanding telegraph and telephone fees.

Telegraph communications are a state-run enterprise. Government and military organs are state organs, and their personnel are public servants. It is beyond doubt that they should pay all telegraph and telephone fees in accordance with the regulations, without the need for repeated government announcements. However, since the outbreak of military conflicts, and because politics has not been on the right track, government and military organs have been sending excessive telegrams and installing excessive telephones, to the point that they cannot pay off their debts. Because the Ministry of Communications cannot recover the fees they owe each year, various improvement and reorganization plans cannot be implemented. The economic losses to the Ministry of Communications are already considerable, but the moral losses are even more regrettable because government and military organs do not send telegrams or install telephones in accordance with the regulations, pay all fees, and then fail to comply with government orders to make monthly payments.

We deeply understand that the state has faced many crises in recent years, and expenditures have been enormous, so government and military organs may not have sufficient funds. However, if we examine the budgets and final accounts of government and military organs, we can see that monthly postal and telegraph fees are clearly listed. If these postal and telegraph fees can be paid monthly, the telegraph authorities will welcome it. If these fixed fees are begrudged and not paid, it seems that the claim of insufficient funds cannot be considered a reasonable excuse for government and military organs.

An examination of the telegrams sent by government and military organs reveals that many of them are indeed urgent, but many are also ordinary matters. Even among urgent telegrams, some are deliberately ostentatious, and some are unnecessarily lengthy. This is what is meant by sending excessive telegrams. After sending excessive telegrams, the telegraph fees will inevitably be delayed, and after being delayed, they will be difficult to pay off. If government and military organs can comply with Commander-in-Chief Chiang's telegram of December 1932, which stated that "unless absolutely necessary to save money, telegrams must not exceed one hundred characters, unless an especially urgent matter, the words 'immediate arrival' must not be used indiscriminately, and unless an emergency, express mail should be used instead of sending a telegram whenever possible," there will be no excessive telegrams, telegraph fees can be paid, and there will be no accumulation of debts as large as they are today.

The changeover of government and military organs is an internal matter and has nothing to do with the telegraph bureau. Why should they make excuses and refuse to pay the outstanding telegraph and telephone fees of the previous administration? If government and military organs owe money to other organs or stores, can they make such excuses? And if other organs or stores owe money to government and military organs, can they make such excuses? Knowing full well that they cannot make such excuses, but still refusing to pay telegraph and telephone fees, is because government and military organs are accustomed to old habits and neglect government orders, and because the telegraph authorities are intimidated by power and neglect their duties, failing to collect the outstanding telegraph and telephone fees from the government and military organs on a monthly basis is also a major reason.

Now that the most effective order of the Executive Yuan has been issued, if government and military organs fail to pay their telegraph and telephone fees on a monthly basis, the telegraph authorities can, based on this order, suspend telegraph and telephone services. At the same time, they can report to the Ministry of Communications and then to the Executive Yuan for the legal punishment of the head of the organ. Whether the telegraph authority's finances can be rectified depends on whether government and military organs respect this order.

The Truth About the Dispute Between Wuhu Rice Merchants and the Telegraph Bureau

— Hua

Recently, the China Daily in Nanjing and the Wanjiang and Industrial and Commercial Daily in Wuhu published news about "the Wuhu Telegraph Bureau delaying the delivery of telegrams, being sued by local rice merchants in court, and being required to compensate for losses." The case is as follows: Starting last year, the Anhui Provincial Government levied a rice surtax on rice grains leaving the province. Surtax collection offices were established in various regions of Anhui to be responsible for this task. Later, the office received a telegram order from the Provincial Government to stop the collection and set a deadline to close down. However, because the telegram to stop the collection was delayed by several hours by the Wuhu Telegraph Bureau, several rice merchants paid more than 400 piculs of rice surtax, and their requests for the office to return it were unsuccessful. Therefore, the rice merchants believed that the losses they suffered were entirely due to the delayed delivery of the telegram. They specially jointly hired lawyers to sue the director of the Telegraph Bureau in the Wuhu District Court for negligence and demanded compensation. The reporter feels that whether the losses of the Wuhu rice merchants were entirely due to the delayed delivery of the telegram is, of course, still open to question, but the delayed delivery of the telegram to stop the collection is the main reason for the occurrence of this case, so it is certainly necessary to first examine the necessity. Especially in the midst of the active rectification of the telegraph business, the above unfortunate incident occurred, and it is even more necessary to thoroughly investigate the cause and share it with the community. Now, I will write down the reasons for the delay that the reporter inquired about, hoping that readers of this publication will give fair advice.

Originally, each telegram's receiving place name should only be one place, according to regulations. If there are two receiving place names, then there are two telegrams, and two telegraph fees must be paid. The reason is simple, because a telegram sent to two places requires two sets of labor and materials, and the situation is exactly the same as that of two telegrams with different texts. However, some military and government telegrams often are not subject to this restriction. Each telegram often has several or even a dozen receiving place names. Under special circumstances, the Telegraph Bureau certainly cannot refuse. Unfortunately, the Anhui Provincial Government's telegram to stop the collection of rice surtax was delayed because of the confusion caused by multiple receiving place names. The receiving place name of the telegram of the Wan Provincial Government to stop the collection of rice surtax was written like this: "Wuhu Nanjing Shangxinhe send to Xiliangshan Chuxian send to Chenjiaqian Guangde send to Dingbu Mingguang send to Xuyi Surtax Collection Office." At that time, the Wuhu Telegraph Bureau believed that there was no recipient's name, address, or other identifier between the place names Wuhu and Nanjing, and it was thought that it was "Wuhu Nanjing Shangxinhe sent to Xiliangshan." Because Wuhu is only more than 30 li from Xiliangshan, and Nanjing Shangxinhe is 120 or 130 li from Xiliangshan, and telegrams sent to Xiliangshan have always been sent exclusively by the Wuhu Bureau, it was undoubtedly assigned to a special delivery to Xiliangshan. Later, after the Wuhu Bureau's review staff's research results, they felt that Wuhu itself might also be copying the telegram, so the telegram was re-extracted and sent. But it had been delayed for several hours. That is the reason for the so-called delay.

The reporter expresses his sincere sympathy for the Wuhu rice merchants' major investment loss this time, but is this loss really due to the delayed delivery of the telegram? The content of the Anhui Provincial Government's telegram to stop the collection of rice surtax is, of course, impossible for outsiders to guess, but according to common sense, there must be a clearly specified deadline. It will never say, "Stop collecting from the time the telegram arrives." Moreover, the place to collect rice surtax is not just Wuhu, and of course it will be treated the same as other places in the province. Wuhu must not be allowed to suffer losses alone. This is what I want to ask the Wuhu rice merchants to recognize clearly, otherwise it will be a waste of effort.

I heard that the Ministry of Communications believes that the Wuhu Bureau's delayed telegram delivery, although there are the reasons described above, is still due to the negligence of the office staff. The responsible personnel have been given appropriate punishment and are trying to avoid the occurrence of the same incident. As for whether the Wuhu rice merchants' lawsuit against the Telegraph Bureau is legal and whether the Telegraph Bureau should be held liable for compensation, the court will, of course, handle it impartially based on the Telegraph Regulations of the Ministry of Communications, so there is no need for the reporter to say more!

Notice to Those Who Set Up Academic Experimental Radio Stations

— Ming

Since the Ministry of Communications published announcements in Ping, Lu, Hu, and Han and other places, offering rewards for secretly reporting privately established radio stations, confidential letters have been pouring in, and the number of privately established radio stations that have been detected and seized is not small. However, among them, after investigation, some of the main purposes of setting up stations are purely for experimental research purposes, which are naturally different from ordinary privately established radio stations for secret communication, and cannot be generalized.

The establishment of radio stations by public or private organizations or individuals for academic research purposes is permitted by Article 3, Section 6 of the Telecommunications Regulations. The communications authorities even promulgated the Regulations for the Establishment of Academic Experimental Wireless Radio Stations in July of last year. At that time, the regulations were also consulted by various relevant agencies and groups for reference. Therefore, the Ministry of Communications' supervision and encouragement of the establishment of academic experimental wireless radio stations (hereinafter referred to as experimental radio stations) cannot be denied. However, since the implementation of these regulations, a year has passed in a blink of an eye. Many experimental radio stations in various places have complied with the regulations and applied for registration, but many are still waiting to see. The communications authorities are not responsible for guaranteeing the safety of these unregistered experimental radio stations. Once someone reports them and it is confirmed, in order to maintain the authority of the law, they will inevitably be banned and brought to justice. It is hoped that those who set up experimental radio stations will quickly register and obtain licenses in accordance with the regulations, and no longer hesitate and linger, so as to avoid falling into the legal net, so that they can concentrate on wireless radio research and experimentation.

The Regulations for the Establishment of Academic Experimental Wireless Radio Stations have 26 articles, which are quite complete. Now, the contents are summarized as follows, for reference by relevant parties:

(A) A radio station that aims to study wireless telecommunications academics and is dedicated to experimentation and testing is called an academic wireless radio station. This type of radio station can be established by national universities and colleges, specialized science and engineering schools and science and engineering societies legally registered with the education authorities of the National Government, and citizens of the Republic of China who are engaged in wireless telecommunications research and improvement and can make practical contributions, after applying for and being approved by the Ministry of Communications. When applying, the following items should be opened in detail: (1) Name, resume, and address of the person in charge and the person in charge of the experiment; (If there is any change in this personnel, it should be reported to the Ministry of Communications at any time.) (2) The registration authority of private schools or societies, and the year and month of registration; (3) The name, address, organization, estimate, and source of the radio station, the machine program, and the engineering plan.

(B) The transmission power of the transmitter of the experimental radio station shall not exceed 50 watts for personal installations; for installations by societies or national and private specialized schools, the maximum shall not exceed 100 watts. The frequency of the radio waves used by the telecommunications machine shall be limited to the following, and should be kept stable as much as possible so that the difference from the original frequency does not exceed two per thousand, and the occurrence of multiple waves must be avoided:

(1) 56,000-60,000 kHz (wavelength 5.35-5 meters)

(2) 28,000-30,000 kHz (wavelength 10.7-10 meters)

(3) 14,000-14,400 kHz (wavelength 21.4-20 meters)

(4) 7,000-7,300 kHz (wavelength 42.8-41 meters)

(5) 3,500-4,000 kHz (wavelength 85-75 meters)

(6) 1,715-2,000 kHz (wavelength 175-150 meters)

(C) The experimental radio station should be installed within six months after being approved for establishment, and the machine program, detailed wiring diagram, transmission power, maximum antenna current and its height, radio wave method and its frequency, communication method and the address, call sign, wave and power of its communication radio station, and the daily transmission time, etc. should be submitted to the Ministry of Communications for inspection, issuance of a license, and designation of a call sign. The above items shall not be changed by themselves after being stipulated or approved by the Ministry of Communications.

(D) The experimental radio station shall not be used for any other communication or broadcasting purposes other than for academic experimental purposes; it shall not disturb or interfere with the communication of the land, sea, and air forces, and the business of state-run or public communication organs; it shall not intercept the communication of other radio stations. If it is accidentally acquired, it must be kept absolutely confidential, but this restriction does not apply in the event of a distress call.

(E) When the experimental radio station communicates with other radio stations, it should fill in the form for the academic experimental radio station communication record in detail according to the format stipulated by the Ministry of Communications, and send it to the Ministry of Communications for inspection every quarter. The results of peacetime experiments must be summarized and reported at the end of May and November each year.

(F) The Ministry of Communications may send personnel to inspect the machine parts, licenses, and various related books and charts of the radio station at any time, and the radio station shall not refuse on any pretext. If any violation of the rules is found, the experiment may be suspended or the license revoked for a period of time depending on the severity of the circumstances, and the provisions of Article 21 of the Telecommunications Regulations may be followed.

The above six items are a brief description of the content of the regulations. Readers who want to see the whole picture can directly write to the Telecommunications Department of the Ministry of Communications in Nanjing or to this newspaper to request a copy, which will be sent immediately.

Advantages of the Newly Revised Public Telegram Fee Payment Method (Continued)

— Baozhen

(4) After a sender has dispatched a telegram, should they discover that essential information has been omitted from the message, or that a character has been transcribed incorrectly, or mistranslated, or if they receive a paid public telegram from the receiving telegraph office inquiring about a doubtful character in the telegram, and after investigation, it is confirmed to be their own error, they may request the telegraph office to send a paid public telegram to notify the receiving telegraph office to supplement the message or correct the erroneous character. The fee for this type of paid public telegram is only charged according to the number of characters requested by the applicant. For example, if supplementing two characters for an address or the text of the message, only the fee for two characters needs to be paid; if correcting one character in the message, only the fee for one character needs to be paid. Compared to the previous practice where the sender had to pay for all the characters contained in the entire telegram, this can also reduce a portion of the telegraph fee.

(5) If a sender is unsure whether a telegram they have sent has been delivered successfully and has doubts, they can go to the telegraph office and request that a paid public telegram be sent on their behalf to inquire about the original telegram, asking on what date and time it was delivered. The fee for sending this public telegram is waived; only the return telegraph fee for six characters needs to be prepaid, and then they can receive a return telegram from the receiving telegraph office indicating the date and time of delivery. Prior to the implementation of the new method, the fee for this type of paid public telegram had to be paid by the sender according to the number of characters contained in the original telegram, and the return telegraph fee also had to be prepaid. Now, only a return telegraph fee for six characters needs to be paid, which is also a benefit for senders.

(6) Senders generally eagerly await a reply from the recipient after sending a telegram. If the receiving party neglects to reply, it is bound to cause anxiety. However, if the sender wants to send another telegram to urge the other party to reply, they would have to pay another telegraph fee, which feels too uneconomical. The new standardized fee payment method for public telegrams now includes a type of paid public telegram that says, "Sender requests that the receiving party be notified to send a reply telegram promptly." If a sender is urgently awaiting a reply to a telegram they sent, but has not received a reply promptly, they can request the telegraph office to send a paid public telegram to the receiving telegraph office to urge the recipient to reply. Upon receiving the public telegram urging a reply, the receiving party will naturally not be able to delay the reply any further. Moreover, the fee for this public telegram is only one character's worth, which saves a considerable amount compared to sending a telegram to urge a reply themselves. This is indeed one of the advantages of the newly revised fee payment method for public telegrams.

(7) Suppose a business in Qingdao has just sent a telegram to a foreign firm or manufacturer in Shanghai ordering a batch of goods. Subsequently, they hear reliable news in the market that the price of these goods is showing a continuous and sharp downward trend. If they were to order based on the current market price, they would inevitably suffer an unexpected loss when the goods arrive. To remedy this, the only option is to stop the telegram that has already been sent. If a sender encounters the above situation, they do not need to send another telegram directly to the receiving party to make a statement. Instead, they can entrust the telegraph office to send a paid public telegram to notify the receiving telegraph office to cancel the telegram. The telegraph office only charges the fee for one character for this type of public telegram, which can be considered extremely low and provides great convenience to the sender. Furthermore, if the sender requires the receiving telegraph office to reply with confirmation that the original telegram has been cancelled, they can also do so, but they must prepay the return telegraph fee for six characters so that the receiving telegraph office can reply to the sending telegraph office after cancelling the original telegram. The cost to the sending party is only these six characters' worth of return telegraph fee, and since the telegram they sent has already been confirmed by the receiving telegraph office as having been cancelled, unexpected disputes can be avoided.

(8) Suppose a telegram is sent to Qingyuan, and the telegraph office notifies that the telegram cannot be delivered because the recipient has gone to Beijing. If the sender knows the recipient's address in Beijing and is willing to bear the forwarding fee for the original telegram, they can ask the telegraph office to send a paid public telegram to notify the Qingyuan telegraph office to forward the telegram to Beijing. Regardless of the number of characters, this public telegram only requires the fee for six characters, which is also quite inexpensive.

Based on the above points, the promulgation of the standardized fee payment method for public telegrams undoubtedly provides great convenience for both senders and recipients. From now on, if senders or recipients want to inquire with the other party's telegraph office about any matter related to a telegram they have received or sent, or to notify the other party's telegraph office, they can utilize paid public telegrams instead of sending telegrams themselves, thus avoiding unnecessary telegraph fees. Furthermore, this newly revised method applies equally to both domestic and international telegrams. Once senders and recipients understand how to use paid public telegrams, they will save even more on international telegrams. From this, it can be seen that the Telegraph Administration Department of the Ministry of Communications has recently made all arrangements for telegraph services with the aim of facilitating the public and strives to provide thorough service.

Recent Rectification of Broadcasting Stations by the Ministry of Communications

— Yuzhou

In recent years, the number of broadcasting stations in various parts of our country has been increasing, and the number of people using radios is even greater. In bustling city thoroughfares, one cannot escape the noisy songs, and even in the countryside near cities, bamboo poles are often seen erected, each with a radio antenna. The Ministry of Communications believes that the broadcasting industry is of great importance to a nation's politics and culture. Furthermore, in our country, where public intelligence is undeveloped and only a small number of ordinary people have the ability to read and newspapers, the promotion of social education, the dissemination of common knowledge, and the transmission of important news all rely on the assistance of broadcasting stations. In order to achieve proper effects and avoid unexpected drawbacks, it attaches great importance to broadcasting stations. Previously, because our country's broadcasting industry was still in its infancy, a certain degree of leniency had to be granted for the sake of promotion. Now that the situation is different, strict principles should be adopted for rectification. The recent rectification situation is described in detail below, which is likely to be welcome news for those who are concerned about the broadcasting industry.

(1) Suspension of Issuing Permits. The Ministry of Communications stipulates that the frequencies used for broadcasting stations are from 550 kHz to 1500 kHz, and the difference between each frequency should be 10 kHz. Therefore, in fact, a total of more than 90 stations can be established. Now, the Ministry of Communications believes that these frequencies have been fully allocated, and the established stations are in need of consolidation. Therefore, last month, it stipulated that the issuance of permits for privately-operated broadcasting stations should be uniformly suspended, and this was published in major newspapers in Beijing and Shanghai, which readers are presumably aware of. However, what we should still pay attention to is that the purpose of this suspension of issuing permits by the Ministry of Communications is purely to rectify broadcasting stations, and it should not be mistaken as an unwarranted restriction on privately-operated telecommunications businesses. The reason is that since the wavelengths have already been fully allocated, if more stations continue to be established, interference will inevitably occur, and even the established broadcasting stations will experience difficulties in broadcasting.

(2) Banning Poorly Managed Stations. After a broadcasting station is approved for establishment, the Ministry of Communications still conducts strict inspections at any time. Regarding equipment, it appoints specialists to go to each station for on-site inspections. Regarding programs, the International Telecommunications Bureau and the Tianjin Telegraph Bureau pay attention to listening in the South China and North China regions, respectively. Those who are poorly managed are punished accordingly, and those with serious circumstances are banned. Recently, more than ten stations have been banned. Some were banned because they failed to establish the station within the time limit after being approved. Others were banned because of faulty equipment and repeated orders to improve it were not followed. Still others were banned for broadcasting obscene and lewd songs and failing to comply with orders to be punished. Others were banned for privately transferring or subletting the station. All of these items are clearly stipulated in the "Provisional Regulations for Banning Privately-Operated Wireless Broadcasting Stations" promulgated by the Ministry of Communications, and broadcasting stations that violate regulations and disobey guidance are subject to banning, which is their own fault.

(3) Rectifying the Broadcasting Programs of Each Station. The Ministry of Communications has already made principled regulations regarding the broadcasting programs of each station in the "Provisional Regulations for Banning Privately-Operated Wireless Broadcasting Stations." However, the stations often neglect this. Recently, the Ministry of Communications issued a notice to all stations, stating that on the negative side, they must not cater to the low-level interests of all sectors of society and must not broadcast obscene and lewd songs that harm public morals. On the positive side, for the sake of promoting Party principles, raising the level of people's knowledge, and inspiring national spirit, they should allocate a considerable amount of time each day to broadcast Party principles, short biographies of national heroes of past dynasties, common knowledge of citizenship, international common knowledge, and the good morals inherent in our country, etc. All reports should be mainly in Mandarin. At the same time, each station was ordered to submit a copy of its current broadcasting schedule, and any subsequent changes should be reported five days in advance for the convenience of verification. In addition, one more thing is worth reporting. The Ministry of Communications plans to conduct a thorough study after collecting the broadcasting schedules of each station, and make specific regulations regarding the programs that general broadcasting stations should have and the allocation of time for them, so that each station has something to comply with. The quality of broadcasting programs is directly related to the actual effectiveness of broadcasting stations, so it is necessary to rectify them seriously.

In summary, the Ministry of Communications' hard work in rectifying broadcasting stations is clearly evident. However, there is something we must say. Our country's broadcasting industry is disorganized, and in the past, due to the relationship between local jurisdictions, it was difficult to manage, resulting in a rather chaotic situation, and there were many complaints in society. Now, through the Ministry of Communications' efforts to rectify it, it has gradually become more standardized, and if it can continue to move forward in this way, the future is promising. It is deeply hoped that Party and government agencies will direct their self-established broadcasting stations to be subject to the command of the Ministry of Communications in accordance with the law, so that the effect of overall planning can be achieved, and that all privately-operated broadcasting stations should recognize the importance of their responsibilities, which are different from running ordinary businesses, and must strive to improve themselves within the scope of laws and regulations.

A Noteworthy Ten Million Yuan

— You

The amount of international telegraph fees saved for the public after the opening of international wireless communications.

Since the establishment of the International Telegraph Administration in 1929, the rates for telegrams between our country and various parts of the world have been reduced through repeated negotiations. By the end of March of this year, the public had saved nearly ten million yuan in telegraph fees as a result. The detailed figures are listed in the table below:

Those who pay attention to telegram matters may sometimes question the savings in telegraph fees due to the increase in the silver dollar price of international telegrams. It is noted that this increase is determined in accordance with international telecommunications regulations based on changes in the exchange rate of the gold franc. When the exchange rate fluctuates, the silver dollar price must inevitably increase or decrease accordingly. However, regardless of whether this silver dollar price increases or decreases, if the standard gold franc price (see item 1 in the table) has never been reduced (item 2 in the table is the reduced price), then all sectors of society would have added a burden of ten million yuan to international wireless telegraph fees. The so-called savings in telegraph fees refers to this. As for why the communications authorities negotiate with all parties to reduce prices, it is because the telecommunications industry serves the public and cannot have profit as its sole purpose. Therefore, even in the midst of extreme difficulties in the telecommunications economy, it still reduces prices as much as possible to lighten the public's burden, which is worthy of praise by the people of the country.

Recent Trends in the Development of World Telecommunications Technology

— Wang Dachun

In recent years, the telecommunications industry in various countries around the world has seen remarkable technological developments. In particular, since last year—1934 in the Western calendar—there has been significant progress in telecommunications technology, making telecommunications transmission more efficient and rapid. All the communication methods that telecommunications engineers once considered to be only in the realm of ideals have now gradually reached the point of practical application. In short, the communication methods of the telecommunications industry in various countries, whether in wired or wireless communications, are tending to use higher frequencies. Now, when we try to study the various communication methods recently adopted by various countries, what is most noteworthy is that the communication channels within various communication methods often contain broad bands of frequency. For example, the multi-channel telephone system used in European countries last year had broad bands of frequency available for application because its circuit was equipped with newly designed feed-back amplifiers and crystal filterer, which resulted in excellent performance in communication. There have been many such technological developments to date, and although the results are different, they have all achieved satisfactory success.

Now, let us first describe the more important progress of the telecommunications technology of various countries in the past year. Among them, the use of the carrier telephone system on overhead lines is more well-known because it uses broad bands of frequency to create supplementary communication channels, and the width of the frequency bands can also be used to transmit the broadcasting programs of broadcasting stations. This method was put into practical use between Bratislava and Cosice in Czechoslovakia in August of last year, that is, adding a high communication channel to the original three communication channels, and the bandwidth of the high communication channel was 7,500 cycles.

Adding a large number of communication channels to the original telecommunications circuit is a more meaningful event in the development of telecommunications technology in the past year. The method is to add ten voice frequency telegraphs to each of the original standard three-communication channel carrier methods in the telegraph machine circuit. In this way, together with the original telephone communication channels, up to 54 two-way telegraph communication channels will be added on one circuit of overhead lines. This installation method has been implemented in Cape Town and lohannesburg in South Africa, and the distance between the two ends can reach 1,000 miles.

Telecommunications circuits, telephone repeaters, and Loading Coils, etc., all of the latest designs can provide more than one telephone circuit for use. Therefore, the ingenuity of the new design is that a carrier circuit can often be added to each ordinary telephone circuit, and its frequency band can be used from 3,500 cycles to 7,000 cycles. The newly installed cables between London and Glasgow are designed according to this, and the amount of communication can be greatly increased in practice. From this, it can be seen that it is no longer difficult to add a single-channel carrier channel to an ordinary telephone circuit. Now, we are further studying the use of high-speed carrier communication channels of more than three channels in extremely long-distance circuits, and the realization of this is expected to be not far away. Recently, a submarine cable was newly designed and manufactured between Australia and Tasmania Island, and its communication channels are numerous. The total width of all frequency bands is planned to use 42,500 cycles. The mechanical equipment at both ends is also specially designed so that each single line can bear three two-way telephone communication channels with a frequency band of 9,000 cycles; three one-way telephone communication channels with a frequency band of 11,000 to 20,000 cycles; three reply communication channels with a frequency band of 21,000 to 31,000 cycles: In addition, there is one replaceable broadcast communication channel with a frequency level of 34,000 to 42,500 cycles.

As for land cables, in 1933, the city of Morristown, New Jersey, USA, conducted several experiments that were of great significance: the method was to connect each pair of underground cable core wires 25 miles long to each other at the front and rear ends. In this way, the core wires were hypothetically made into a line circuit 850 miles long. Using a frequency rate of 4 to 40 kilo cycles (KC), nine carrier telephone communication channels can be obtained. The application of coaxial lines for communication methods (a coaxial line is a hollow circular conductor tube with a thinner wire placed in the tube, and its function is that it can transmit telegrams, telephones, or television symbols in a very wide frequency level) can transmit even wider frequency bands. Various countries are currently studying it, and the results of the experiments can be used to effectively and smoothly transmit frequency bands with a width of more than 1,000 kilo cycles. If appropriate equipment is used, this frequency level can be divided into 200 one-way telephone communication channels. However, on coaxial lines, the amount of communication attenuation will increase with the widening of the frequency level, and the distance between the machines in the circuit must be shortened. Therefore, the shortening of the distance can reduce the number of repeaters used at the intermediate stations. In the circuit using coaxial lines, each repeater at the intermediate station only needs two pieces, and the number has been reduced, making technical management easier. (To be continued)

Short Biographies of World Telecommunications Inventors

— Jian

Sixteen, Tesla

Mr. Tesla was an American electrical and radio expert. Born in Smiljan, Yugoslavia in 1857. He studied at universities such as Graz and Prague. He then worked for the Austrian Telegraph Company. In 1884, he went to the United States to work as an assistant to Edison. He specialized in the study of high-frequency and high-voltage alternating current. He is most famous for inventing polyphase alternating current method. Rotating magnetic field AC motor. Arc lamp. Tesla transformer. And various wireless electrical components with control settings.

Seventeen, Pupin, Michael

Mr. Pupin. American wireless radio author. Born in Hungary in 1858, he immigrated to the United States at the age of ten, and then studied at Columbia University. Later, he also studied at Cambridge University in England. In 1891, he was appointed professor of mathematics and physics at Columbia University. He conducted important research and exploration on wireless telegraphs and telephones there. He also created a variety of machine parts related to telephones and wireless radios. Mr. Pu devoted himself to the study of resonance. And design wireless circuits with excellent selectivity.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talks

Marrying Eighty Wives in Five Years

— Si

A国民社 report from Belgrade on the 11th stated that Mania, who married a total of eighty wives in five years, has been arrested in the Romanian capital. Mania is only 28 years old. It is said that he spent US$200,000 to marry eighty wives, but after marriage, he would defraud the women of money and then abandon them. This is truly a scandalous case worth noting.

I carefully considered it for him. Marrying eighty wives in five years, averaging almost one bride every twenty days. His means of seducing the opposite sex are so brilliant that they are truly shocking to modern people. However, according to his claims, he would defraud the girls of money immediately after marriage and then abandon them. He spent US$200,000 to marry eighty wives. Then it is clear that he used marriage as a means and defrauding money as the purpose. He married eighty women and spent as much as US$200,000. Then those women who were deceived by him must have spent twice as much as he did. It can be asserted that this is truly the number one gigolo.

Mania's character, although the telegram is brief and does not explain it, but judging from the greatness of his magic to attract women, he must be a young and handsome gigolo. But rather than saying that Mania's means of stealing jade are brilliant, it is better to say that the intellectual level of these women is weak. If a woman marries someone, how can she not consider the opponent's personality, character, knowledge, background, and commit herself to marriage at first sight? Their stupidity is truly immeasurable.

Bigamy is a crime. Not only does our country have some regulations, but the laws of other countries are also like this. Now, Mania has committed seventy or eighty counts of bigamy. I don't know how the judge will rule on the case. I am afraid that there are no such provisions in the law, and there are no such precedents in fact. The judge trying the case is also a difficult problem. Our country is known as the place where gigolos are produced. Although they have played many romantic and tragic histories in society, if compared with Mr. Mania's case, they are really just a drop in the bucket.

Since Adam and Eve committed a catastrophic disaster, the world has added a lot of romantic grievances between foolish men and women. Some women are fooled by men, and some men are fooled by women. It is difficult to separate and resolve, and it is impossible to clear up. This is originally a mystery of the universe. If someone can break this mystery, society will definitely be much cleaner. Now women, although liberated, there is always an obstacle between men and women. Assuming that men and women can be completely liberated and the mystery of the universe can be completely broken, this kind of disaster will not occur.

But now some people are promoting the idea of separate schools for men and women, etc. On the surface, it seems brighter, but in fact, it is more corrupt. Because the mystery of the universe is not broken, it becomes more mysterious, which simply makes the mystery more mysterious and the grievances more aggrieved. As the saying goes, private salt is more popular the more it is banned, it is just a futile effort.

When Autumn Comes

— Ji Juan

Perhaps everyone knows that with each cycle of seasons, each year, a tragedy called a "natural phenomenon" is playing out:

When the summer sun scorches suffocatingly, and struggles with all its might at the end of its own season, attempting a final, brilliant "last burst" of flame, there, on the horizon, comes a rustling, cold downpour, hitting the ground, like water rats churning, rising, then falling.

The rain continues for several days, and that cool, damp air is so comforting! During this time, the sun of the dog days begins to slowly droop its head, like a wounded tiger, or like a person sinking from youth into middle age. Its flame no longer has the courage and fervor of its youthful days, and instead, it begins to wither and become calm. So, the sky slowly rises, appearing as lonely and vast as the sea; the clouds slowly present more beautiful and ever-changing golden hues; the moon grows clearer and more pure; the atmosphere becomes more sluggish and cool. In this way, nature has completely arranged a world more suitable for middle-aged people. And so, this brown, worldly-wise, and calm autumn finally approaches step by step, silently, like an old man with a walking stick.

Autumn has finally crept in so silently, and the mountains are so blurred, the clouds so distant!

Yes! In the mountains, on the branches, in the corners of the damp brick walls of old foundations, on the tips of branches, on the flags of city shops, in the corner of a person's heart, in every tiny place, the shadows of autumn have been sprinkled little by little. During the day, a gentle breeze blows, and leaves leisurely fall to the ground. At night, a bronze mirror-like moon hangs in the middle of the sky, and unknown insects listen intermittently in the damp corners of the house. People's hearts also turn into a漠然 vast sea, empty and calm, little by little, as if constantly contemplating something, but not knowing what it is; as if listening to a sound, but unable to say what kind of words it is! All that can be felt is: a person's heart, a person's soul, is also gradually aging along with the withering of flowers, trees, and fruits, growing old! From past experience, I know that this is autumn, an autumn built for some sinking souls. Autumn is speechless, silent, and calm. It does not demand the flowery rhetoric of brocade flowers and green leaves from nature, like the young spring day. All it asks for are honest fruits and harvests—the achievements that have grown throughout the year. It just silently stretches out its dry hands, and in the calm voice of an elder, it gives us a terrible demand: "Here! Show me your fruits, you must prove how much you have grown!"

This is a difficult question to answer: autumn brings us a real "Judgment Day," and makes us feel guilty and tremble in a selfless chill!

It is truly difficult to describe, the heart is so lonely and empty! Seeing geese flying south, I really want to ask, what place has a high mountain—a mountain so high it's impossible to measure—I want to climb to the highest peak and make the wildest, most primitive cry to the world, to this whole human realm!

Yes, I really want to have a mad cry: I see the gloomy sun, I see the withered trees, I see the graying hairs on the young people's temples, and finally, in this pile of cruel natural phenomena, I see autumn!

Surprised, why is there that strange and uncomfortable feeling? Perhaps afraid, worried about the irrecoverable withering of some good weather? But this is not accurate; the sky and clouds are still so calm and clear, the weather of "Judgment Day" is not necessarily stormy, but think about that terrible withering…

Nature is selfless, the good days have finally passed, and now it is when autumn comes!

Sun Fuchao

— Shi Weizhi

One of the Character Sketches

Sun Fuchao, according to seniority, I should call him grand-uncle, but because he worked in my house since he was little, and is only a dozen years older than me, calling him grand-uncle seems like a joke. When he heard it, he would either blush and say, "Don't call me that, it sounds awkward," or he would put on an elder's airs, making his voice sound very serious: "Child, be good and don't make trouble, grand-uncle will buy you candy later!"

Before he could finish speaking, he couldn't help but burst out laughing first.

Whether he was blushing and forbidding us to call him grand-uncle, or pretending to be an elder, we were children, and when we were happy, we always liked to call him grand-uncle. Moreover, because he was afraid of us calling him that, we would call him grand-uncle repeatedly, until he agreed to us, and only when he answered us would we all laugh together, making him feel very embarrassed.

He loved to drink wine, he could even skip meals, but he had to have wine with every meal, but he was afraid of my father. Every

Page 20

time he drank, he would always secretly drink behind my father's back. As soon as he heard my father's footsteps coming down from upstairs, he would always hide the wine, and hide the spiced beans, peanuts, and the like that went with the wine in a package in his pocket. He would only take it out to drink when my father went outside. Because of this, he would sometimes hurriedly eat a shallow bowl of rice, and sometimes he wouldn't even eat rice. When he heard my father's footsteps, he would pour the rice into the rice bucket, pick up the empty bowl, and eat the rice crumbs clean, so that my father would always think he had just finished eating. So he would put down the rice bowl and return to his bamboo chair to work.

But although he loved to drink, he advised others that it was best not to drink. He would not be stingy with spiced beans, peanuts, beef, and the like for us, letting us grab and eat as much as we wanted. But the Wu Jia Pi wine or tiger bone papaya wine in his hand, he would never let us drink, which was naturally because he loved wine as much as his life, but he deeply knew the harm of wine.

We don't know when he started to like wine, but we do know the reason why he wanted to drink.

After drinking his fill of wine, he would sing "The Little Widow Visits the Grave" or something while working. He would sing and sing, and in the end, he would always sing the Fengyang Flower Drum, "Other people's wives make silk and cloth, my wife has a pair of big feet," repeatedly,颠倒ing, always singing these two sentences.

His body was very strong, his skin was somewhat brown, and he had a Yellow Tianba tattooed on his chest. He could use his two hands to climb to the top of people's awnings without any effort.

In our eyes, he was optimistic. He wasn't like my father, who never smiled all day long. He was always talking and laughing all day long. When he was tired of laughing or talking, he would start drinking, as if drinking could forget some worries.

The family often sent letters, and he would always secretly ask me to read them to him. The letters always asked him for money. After listening, he would always silently tear the letters to pieces, and then drink wine again, and sing "The Little Widow Visits the Grave" and "Fengyang Flower Drum". When singing, or when drinking, he would sometimes suddenly remember something and say to me softly: "Don't tell your father that there are letters from home again."

Gradually, I knew that he had a family he didn't love, and a wife he didn't love.

I remember when my father wanted to fulfill my lifelong wish, he once mustered up the courage to protest to my father: "This is a lifelong matter, you have to be careful." Behind my back, he secretly asked me: "Do you like this marriage? Don't be shy, it's hard to find a wife!"

Later, I left home and went everywhere with my wife, whom I didn't love, to find food. I hadn't heard from him for a long time.

Recently, I heard news about him, saying: Fuchao is crazy, his body is going crazy from drinking, becoming foolish and demented, crying and laughing unpredictably. If he has money, he still goes to drink, and if he doesn't have money, he steals things when he sees them.

Leisure and Clouds

— Cheng Quan

The weather is gradually getting cooler, and autumn seems to be just around the corner again. At dusk, I return with a body covered in slight sweat and a lot of fatigue: Heavens! Maybe this is a bit of life's punishment? However, is true life really a fault, a sin? Why? The saints haven't said that, the gods haven't said that: the society said that! Yes, and there is…

Okay, let it treat life as a fault, let it punish and abuse the countless offenders in various ways; what I want to continue to say is that in the crime of the day, at night, with a wounded and tired body, I say, I actually have a little rest, a little real rest and leisure!

I sit down in the dark house, light a strong-flavored cigarette, let it catch fire, and the smoke rises thread by thread, thread by thread, rises and disappears. Then, I see the clouds outside the window! Those clouds that are always floating in the blue sky, like smoke!

(Clouds like smoke! Piles of them, floating in the vast sky like a colored canvas that has caught fire: crimson gold, bright red, violet! All are so full, so full of the essence of life! Layers upon layers, as vast as the wild mountains and passes. A person—a wandering person—easily misses his hometown, and clearly points out from the color of the clouds which one has floated over from the sky of his hometown. So, give it a thousand sounds of cherish! However, it is indifferent, wandering, and finally, in the constant drifting, it itself is constantly changing into the past. Yes, the clouds are changing!)

Changing! Like being pricked by a needle, I jump up suddenly! I no longer dare to trust my own reason; however, what's the use, the mirror of truth will show my own wrinkled face and pale temples; the life of youth is getting old day by day, the world has gone so far (maybe forward, maybe backward, but who knows?), in short, life is drifting, and it has also changed like a cloud!

Just like a cloud, drifting over from the gray sky of life, how did youth go? How did laughter disappear from the heart? All of this has become completely blurred like a dream of yesteryear. Moreover, it takes even greater adventurous courage to recall them—isn't a heavy footstep stepping forward step by step in the distance, in a vague distance, not long ago? Sluggish, gray, hitting people's hearts, like the drums in a funeral procession, it takes people to an unknown place. I thought of it! That's middle age! That's old age! That's death!

All are illusion! Life, who can deny that it is constantly changing in drifting like clouds?

Changing, until the coming of the night, using its black mourning dress to cover the earth, to cover the entire world!

There was a time when I read Longfellow's "Song of Life", the heavy footsteps of that life were felt: "From the soil you came! You will return to the soil!" But now, life is changing like clouds, drifting, what is hanging in front of a young child is no longer a lush green leaf a second later, but a brown-gray middle-aged curtain!

What kind of mood will follow? As if an old boatman on a small wooden boat has received a premonition of the wind and waves in the sea, waiting curiously, preparing, but constantly trembling.

Looking at the clouds, I felt as cold and disappointed as if I had sunk into an ice cave. I seemed to see the withered face of life and hear its gradually weakening pulse! What life gives people is only a cluster of intangible emptiness like the clouds in the sky, a change as dreamlike as a dream!

(The cigarette has already burned to the end of the butt, and what remains are some ashes of destruction!)

Leisure time is for watching the clouds, but today, finally, leisure has brought unspeakable horror. It's foolish!

(The night has come!)

I am afraid, I even dare not fall asleep, I know: tonight's dream will definitely be a terrible one again.

I decided, I will never look at the clouds again.

Emotions of a Galloping Horse

— Zhen

Again, "End of the Century! End of the Century!"

When I even have to search for the food to fill my stomach today in the dark corners of the beautiful city, I let out such a heavy sigh, and at the same time, the strings of my heart are fully drawn, as complex, urgent, and chaotic as a quartet, and even my nervous system feels a little swollen!

My emotions are mixed with a lot of the element of fire, which manipulates my joy, anger, sorrow, and joy. In one moment I am laughing, in the next moment I am crying. Sometimes I just stare blankly and think inexplicably, as if I have the responsibility to think of something to shift the difficult problem that makes me laugh and cry, but what to think of? ——In the blink of an eye, those difficult problems that make me laugh and cry still come at me.

I look up at the sky, the sky is wooden like my brain nerves, a few wandering clouds, at the lowest, are only still breathing with me! I run around the room, the room is naturally small, I think even if it were bigger, it wouldn't be able to contain my huge and unparalleled resentment, because the vast and boundless sky is also pitifully small in front of me, it is really small, even a place for my knees to rest has become a luxury.

The road has become the playground for my emotions, the tune is impassioned, it competes with the gale, crosses the Himalayas and the Alps Plateau, crosses the only ocean system on the earth, and also wanders through the star systems listed in the sky. The soul unknowingly and seemingly intentionally leaves this body that can only be considered un-stiff, I am thinking, heaven and earth are only a humble and narrow poor hut, I can't find anything of "me" at all, I want to go outside the sky, there is an extra desire to discover the paradise in the outside world. But when my soul and body reunite, I realize that my white-haired top, which is as white as the phlegm I spit out, and my top hat are covered with banana peels and melon seeds that were thrown down from the upper foreign buildings at some unknown time. I hate them, I drive them away ——One grain at a time.

I didn't get to the sky after all ——Very clearly I am still in the world, everything in front of me will not deceive me. I sweep my famine-stricken pupils towards the small stalls with scaly combs, and the unique fragrances that are too much to take in prick my sense of smell, and I drool as I accept them, but when I look back around me, there are still many people drooling, I am not lonely anymore, in the vast universe, my life is not lonely, fragile, and desperately desolate.

I completely returned to harmony with a lingering mood, and from my sweat-soaked back, I suddenly felt a clear and faint coolness. When I turned around, it was an old man who had been abandoned by the "prosperous age" and was flashing with hungry eyes like me ——I call him that is instinctive, not at all an excessive compliment, and he has that palm fan, and he also has one more production tool than me, he is really richer than me, but he is only fanning my top that only contains one copper coin, which is really an odd injustice! But he is still fanning without feeling and enthusiastically, his steps following my speed, and the opening and closing of the fan also coincides with the expansion and contraction of my lungs, "A gentleman helps others achieve their beauty", so a copper coin also gently bids me farewell

And he went behind two fashionable girls again, fanning, fanning, but the wind silk only fluttered the lower end of their cheongsams, not invading their "charitable" heart garden, and at the same time, it was clear that the fanning did not have the magic power of Yonghonglin and the cold air to drive away the fire element; and they seemed to be even more stingy than me, not even leaving a copper coin for the old man. But he was not tired, not annoyed at all, and turned

Page 21

Page 22

Page 23

his face to the gentleman in the long gown there, he was chasing out, struggling, relying on that only tool, it seemed that he wanted to live a happy and thorough life.

But what do I have? ——I think; yes, I am still not empty-handed, I have painless and worry-free hands and feet, I have a heart that the law can't control, thinking of this, my emotions are like a galloping horse flying over again, but not the vast outside world, but the realistic harmony.

"From the hands of the devil, save the people of the spiritual world. 'No matter who, as long as they continue to work hard, we can make them transcendent'. Heaven also has loving sympathy, and all the gods sincerely welcome him".

Goethe transformed the angel in "Faust" and sang like this, and I also sing like this, and I blindly believe it.

Broadcast Program

New Song Introduction

A Sight of Desolation

(1) Society is so licentious, people's hearts are so decadent, look up and see a sight of desolation! The room is full of colors, the room is full of the smell of meat, I don't know how many young people are buried!

(2) If you have hands and don't apply them, it's the same as not having hands; Demon Palace! My husband, was buried alive by you! If you have legs and don't go upwards, it's the same as not having legs, Demon Palace! My husband, was buried alive by you! The red lights of the year are brilliantly shining, numbing the heart; the thick smell of wine, the fragrance of meat, fascinated his ambition; lost his children, all hope; brought back, a series of resentments and annoyances; look up, a sight of desolation, lower your head, the world is full of vicissitudes!

(3) If you have a brain and don't think, it's the same as not having a brain; without a brain, it's the same as being disabled, everything has become despair! If you have strength and don't work, it's the same as being disabled and paralyzed; only enjoy! Can't last long, life is only sad! Love songs are singing together, beautiful songs are leisurely, covering his thoughts; the dance of eyebrows, the release of color, buried his strength; young people! The country is in trouble; it's not the time for singing and dancing! Young people! Open your eyes and take a look! A sight of desolation!

Movie News

Microphone Broadcasts

The "Performing Arts Laboratory" founded by Lu Shi and Liu Yawei is said to have been ordered to be banned by the Education Bureau due to its unsound organization.

Zhang Shichuan and Hu Die of the Mingxing Film Company yesterday convened a meeting of all actors to discuss the methods to be carried out for the Aviation Arts Fair because of its date.

The location shooting of the new era's "Mr. Wang Goes to the Countryside" has been completed, and the protagonist Huang Naishuang returned to Shanghai from Suzhou yesterday.

Cartoonist Wan Laiming, Gu Chan, after arriving in Beijing (Chao Chen has not gone), are quite welcomed by the literary and art circles and relatives and friends, and are very busy with social engagements. It is said that the Central Film Studio also hosted a banquet to entertain them, and plans to hire them to produce a cartoon film.

Xu Xinfu's "Emerald Horse" is a full-fledged detective and martial arts masterpiece. Yesterday, the scene of detective pursuit was filmed, which was quite exciting, especially the shooting of real guns, which was daunting.

Shu Xiuwen and Mei Xi are busy rehearsing the play "Heroes and Beauties" these days. It is said that the director is Ying Yunwei, but the name under which it will be performed in the future will probably not escape the scope of the "Stage Association."

The "Film Tea Party" in Shanghai will die after two or three sessions, and the "Film Tea Party" in Nanjing has not moved after the eighth session. Now Peiping is also preparing a "Film Tea Party," and its fate is unknown.

The "Shanghai Evening News" recently plans to cancel "Volcano Silver Island" and open up a film, drama, and broadcasting section to enrich the content.

Hu Die Sells "Evening Primrose"

"Evening Primrose" now has only one scene left, the dance hall scene, which is about to be completed.

Yesterday, in the Mingxing photography studio, the last scene of the dance hall was filmed, and Hu Die stood at the door of the dance hall selling "Evening Primrose."

On this day, young master Sun Min had an appointment with a girlfriend to dance, but she missed the appointment and came with another man, and they were particularly intimate. This was really enough to make Sun Min angry. He ran out of the dance hall in hatred. At this time, Hu Die was selling "Evening Primrose" at the front door. As soon as he discovered Hu Die's appearance, not only did he not find it annoying, but he also expressed a special affection for her, giving her a large roll of banknotes and only buying a "Evening Primrose" from her.

After this scene was filmed, Hu Die said with a smile: "A flower can sell for so much money, it would be great if I really sold Evening Primrose."

Talking About Wang Ying and Shi Chao's Acting Skills

"The Goddess of Liberty" is about to be released, and for Wang Ying, it can be said to be her most successful work on the screen, and it is also the first sound in the sound film movement. According to her, "The Goddess of Liberty" moved her too much. The entire plot is like a true depiction of her life. In the photography studio, she forgot that she was acting. The joys and sorrows, partings and reunions, joys and angers, songs and cries on the screen are her inner outpouring of passion. She thinks that life will never be so real again. This is what prompted her acting skills to reap a deeper level of harvest. As for Shi Chao, he is one of the new talents selected by Dian Tong in 1935. In the year of the sound film movement, Dian Tong had great hopes for him. This time, in "The Goddess of Liberty," he plays a passionate revolutionary youth. His agile movements, pure emotions, and indomitable spirit realistically portray the personality of the characters in the play.

Mr. Zheng Zhengqiu's Memorial Service Will Be Held at the Lake Society on the 25th

The memorial service for Mr. Zheng Zhengqiu has been in preparation by various groups for a long time. Yesterday, the Chaozhou Shanghai Association of Fellow Townsmen convened a meeting of various groups to discuss and decided to hold it at the Lake Society on Beijing Road on the 25th of this month.

"Games of Love" Released

"Games of Love" is the first collaboration between child stars Freddie Thomas and Helen Parrish, and has achieved extraordinarily amazing results, not inferior to Freddie Bartholomew (who played David's childhood) in "David Copperfield," and the story is quite thought-provoking. At the same time, the specially screened cartoon masterpiece "Little Birds on Sticks" and the slapstick short film "Future Law" are both top-notch quality, and are now being released in Nanjing. The image on the left is a scene from "Games of Love."
